Upon hearing her son’s words, Old Woman Shi suddenly thought, "If my son wants to buy sheep and wine, it would indeed be a token of filial piety, but there’s no need to spend our own silver. When Master Zhou cast that divination, he charged one tael and three *fen*. If his prediction proved false, he would repay tenfold. Why not go ask Master Zhou for the silver first, then buy the sheep and wine with it? Wouldn’t that be better? But Miss Ren told me explicitly never to mention her name. If we go to Master Zhou for the silver and he asks how you returned, what should we say in reply?" Shi Zongfu said, "Mother, set your mind at ease. Just say I made it back on my own. How would he know it was the Ren family who saved me?"

Mother and son settled on their plan, then took their morning meal. Locking the door behind them, they made their way together to the divination market. By then, Master Zhou had already cast ten divinations, and only Peng Jian remained at the entrance, putting away the signboard. Old Woman Shi called out to him. Peng Jian turned his head, saw her, and said, “Old Sister, what brings you here again?” Before the words were fully out, he suddenly caught sight of Shi Zongfu standing beside his mother and started in alarm: “My good brother! Are you man or ghost? What day is it that you’ve returned—whose life are you after?” Shi Zongfu feigned ignorance and forced a smile: “How has Master Peng been? We parted only half a year ago, and now you jest with me. Please go inside and tell him: we’d like the fee for those two divinations from yesterday.” Hearing this, Peng Jian understood at once. Stepping closer with a grin, he said, “Good brother, you’re back. Were you safe and sound last night at the third watch? Since my master’s divination proved false, you and your mother have come to demand repayment.” Old Woman Shi, being of an age to know better, quickly interjected, “Master Peng, we’re poor folk—how dare we ask Master Zhou for repayment? We only beg that he return the fee for yesterday’s divination. I borrowed it from someone else, and if I can repay them, we’ll be deeply indebted to Master Zhou’s great kindness!” How Shi Zongfu managed to reclaim the divination fee will be revealed in the next chapter.

**Chapter Six**
*Mother and Son Repay a Debt of Gratitude; Diviner and Servant Ponder the Art of Augury*

A poem reads:
A master’s skill meets a hand that overturns the sky,
In contests of wit, the unexpected may yet lie.
Think not your move the first to strike—
Beware the foe who claims the lead.

Upon hearing Old Woman Shi’s words, Peng Jian knew full well the “fine speech” she and her son had concocted to demand repayment. With a cold laugh, he said, “How amusing! How very amusing! My master can’t very well argue today!” Still chuckling, he stepped inside and called out, “Quickly, return the divination fee to them!”

“I did warn you to examine the divination carefully—you claimed it was ‘never wrong in a hundred cases,’ yet today this very matter has come to pass!” At this, Master Zhou, still seated, rounded on Peng Jian: “Are you mad? What nonsense are you spouting?” Peng Jian grinned. “Nonsense? They’re here to demand tenfold repayment!” Master Zhou flared up. “Rubbish! Who dares demand repayment from me?” Peng Jian replied, “No need for anger, sir. The ones demanding repayment are right outside the door.” Without waiting for further orders, he went out and ushered in Shi Zongfu and his mother.

Master Zhou saw clearly from his seat: it was indeed the widow Shi, with a sturdy fellow standing beside her—her son, no doubt. His heart lurched. “Yesterday I divined that her son would be crushed to death in a ruined kiln at the third watch. How has he returned alive? Their demand for repayment is a minor matter—what troubles me is that my yin-yang calculations were flawless. How could they fail to manifest? There must be some hidden cause.” He addressed the widow from his seat: “Who is this beside you, and what brings you here?” Old Woman Shi answered, “Master, this is my son, Shi Zongfu. He did not die last night and only returned home this morning. I’ve brought him here to kowtow to you.” Quick-witted, Shi Zongfu heard his mother’s words, promptly knelt, and kowtowed once before rising to stand at her side.

That single bow turned Master Zhou’s swarthy face crimson. Shame and embarrassment mingled as he pushed the divination silver across the table. “Widow Shi, I won’t take advantage of your poverty—take it!” Shi Zongfu stepped forward and gathered up the ten packets of silver. Master Zhou pressed further: “Shi Zongfu, did you spend last night in the ruined kiln south of the city? Who taught you the art that allowed you to break the spell and save your life? Tell me the truth, and I’ll reward you handsomely!” Hearing this interrogation, Shi Zongfu replied, “Last night I was hurrying home and couldn’t reach an inn in time, so I did indeed spend the night in the ruined kiln. Around midnight, my stomach suddenly ached, and I needed to relieve myself. I’d just stepped outside the kiln when it collapsed—so I wasn’t crushed inside.” Master Zhou countered, “Impossible. Yesterday I divined that a heavy rain would fall from the hour of the monkey until the hour of the rooster, clearing only at the third watch. I also divined that you would die alone in the kiln, with no savior. How could you have gone out to defecate? I don’t believe a word of it!”

“‘Master Peng,’ scoffed Peng Jian upon seeing Lord Zhou reimburse Granny Shi, ‘your divination was supposed to be infallible—yet now you’ve suffered a loss! Shi Zongfu truly had a stomachache, and it was a belly full of excrement that saved his life. The silver has already been given to him—let him and his mother go. Why keep pressing him?’ Lord Zhou, stung by these words, hung his head in shame and said nothing. Granny Shi, sensing the shift, promptly took her leave. Peng Jian followed her out. Zongfu then asked, ‘The signboard promised ten taels and three mace—why only ten?’ Hearing this, Peng Jian stamped his foot and said, ‘I’ll make up the three mace myself—wait here while I fetch it.’ Granny Shi quickly interjected, ‘My lord, don’t trouble yourself over such trifles with a child. We’re grateful just to recover our principal. You’ve already compensated tenfold—more than enough. How could we accept further repayment from you?’”

“At the time, Peng Jian found these words hard to bear. Slowly, he said, ‘Good brother, though you spoke without thinking, what you said makes perfect sense. If His Lordship has already compensated, how could I not do the same?’ With that, he reached into his robe and took out ten small packets, handing them to Shi Zongfu. Zongfu, shameless as ever, accepted them. After his mother added a few polite words, the two left in high spirits. Peng Jian stood dumbstruck for a while, then turned and stormed into the inner hall, too furious to speak.

Lord Zhou, already displeased by Peng Jian’s earlier teasing, saw him enter in such a state. He wanted to scold him, but then thought, ‘If I reprimand him now, won’t people laugh and say, “He couldn’t even read his own divination, so he takes it out on others?”’ Swallowing his anger, he said, ‘Peng Jian, go take down the signboard at the gate. From now on, I will no longer sell divinations.’

Seeing Lord Zhou’s anger, Peng Jian dared not disobey. He took down the signboard and returned to store it away. Truly:

*No matter how much water you draw from the Three Rivers,
It cannot wash away today’s shame.*”

At that time, the Shi family mother and son, having received thirteen taels of silver, were overjoyed. They purchased a sheep and wine from the market stalls along the way and returned home. After changing into new clothes, they went together to the Ren household to kowtow and express their gratitude to Elder Ren and his wife. Seeing the weight of their gifts, Elder Ren repeatedly declined, but the Shi mother and son would not hear of it. With no other choice, the elder accepted. He then instructed his servants to prepare a feast to welcome them. After drinking for half a day, they finally took their leave. As they departed, Elder Ren and his wife again and again urged them never to reveal that it was his daughter who had devised the plan to save them.

This matter shall be set aside for now.

As for Lord Zhou, ever since the day the Shi family mother and son had come to reclaim the divination fee, he had been deeply displeased. He shut down his divination stall for several days in a row, refusing to read fortunes for anyone, and instead sat sullenly in his study. He thought to himself, *"My Eight Trigrams are precise, my judgments infallible—how could my divination of Shi Zongfu’s death have been so wrong?"* He pondered further: *"Yet the previous divinations I cast were all accurate."* His heart grew ever more perplexed.

Suddenly, he jolted awake with a start and laughed at himself, saying, *"How foolish I am! Why not cast another divination to see? Then I would know. Why waste time in wild speculation?"* Hurriedly, he took up his divination tube, shook it several times, and cast a hexagram. Upon careful examination, he found it to be *"pure yin holding the position of the self."* His heart leapt in alarm: *"That day when I divined for myself, it was also inauspicious for yin persons—today I cast another hexagram of pure yin! Could some yin person be disrupting my Eight Trigrams?"* He pondered it from every angle, and all signs pointed to this conclusion. Yet try as he might, he could not divine the name of this yin person, and his frustration grew.

*(The narrator adds: Since Peach Blossom Girl had already transmitted her method to Old Woman Shi, her own Eight Characters had long been concealed. How could Lord Zhou possibly deduce Peach Blossom Girl’s name? Thus, no matter how he calculated—palm-reading, reckoning, reckoning, palm-reading—he could discern nothing. Secretly, he seethed: "Once I uncover this person’s name, I swear I will not rest until I have cut them in two!")* In a fit of rage, he flung aside the divination box. After stewing in his anger for some time, with no recourse and no solution, he could only relent.

From that day forward, he sat in gloom all day, nearly forsaking even food and drink. Those around him knew Lord Zhou’s temper well and dared not offer comfort. In the blink of an eye, it was already the first ten days of the seventh month. That day, Lord Zhou sat alone in the flower pavilion.

Peng Jian entered to find Lord Zhou sunk in gloom. Knowing it was over the matter of Shi Zongfu, he burst into laughter and said, "My lord, if Shi Zongfu had never emerged from that ruined kiln, would he not have been crushed to death inside? Perhaps he did some good deed along the way. As the old saying goes, 'A single act of hidden merit may add ten years to one’s lifespan.' It may well be that he encountered some noble soul who secretly came to his aid. Why not divine for yourself to see if this is so?"

Lord Zhou replied, "When have I not divined for myself? The hexagram clearly shows a yin person who rescued him from disaster, breaking my divination. But no matter how I calculate, I cannot deduce that person’s name!"

Peng Jian continued, "In this city of Zhaoge, let alone a yin person—even the most towering of men could hardly disrupt my lord’s divine eight trigrams. Moreover, your calculations have always been infallible, step after step. Even if this one hexagram proves inaccurate, what harm is there? The diviners at the gate have been waiting day after day, their mouths parched from speaking, yet they refuse to leave, pleading endlessly. Some have even come from afar, and if they depart without a divination, they leave in bitter resentment. I deeply regret this. My lord’s divinations were meant to guide the lost. If you abandon this purpose over such a trifle, will you not be ridiculed? What is to be done?"

Lord Zhou pondered his words and said, "What you say is reasonable, but I still wish to uncover the name of the one who rescued Shi Zongfu. Yet no matter how I calculate, the eight trigrams seem unreliable. Let me first divine a hexagram or two for myself to test their accuracy before reopening the divination market. One cannot be too careful!"

Peng Jian smiled and said, "My lord, instead of divining for yourself, why not divine for me? Let us see what fortune or misfortune awaits me in the coming months."

Lord Zhou gave a cold laugh. "Peng Jian, you have served me faithfully for many years, honest and diligent in all things. Today, I shall grant you a divination." He instructed Peng Jian to light incense before the ancient sages and fetch the divination box. Peng Jian, overjoyed, quickly lit a stick of incense and handed over the box. Lord Zhou shook the oracle tube six times in succession, scrutinizing the hexagram within. Suddenly, his expression changed—his tongue flicked, his head shook. Had he not divined that day, all might have been well. But this single hexagram turned Lord Zhou’s dark face sallow, his thick brows knitting with two strands of purple qi.

Truly, no one yet knew what fortune or misfortune this hexagram foretold for Peng Jian, or what omens it bore. But that shall be revealed in the next chapter.

**Chapter Seven: A Trial Divination Reveals Ominous News; A Special Plea Unlocks New Hope**

*Poem:*
Who would have thought Lord Zhou’s trigrams so keen,
Yet Peach Blossom’s art outshines the seer’s sheen.
Even the strong meet stronger hands unseen—
A guide through mist saves old Peng’s doom serene.

Had Lord Zhou not divined for Peng Jian, all might have been well. But once the hexagram was cast, he stood dumbstruck, his complexion shifting. After a long silence, he fixed his gaze on Peng Jian, nodding repeatedly with a sigh of sorrow.

Peng Jian, seeing Lord Zhou’s grim expression after the divination, grew alarmed. "My lord," he asked, "does this hexagram foretell more misfortune than fortune? Why not explain it so I may take precautions?"

Lord Zhou let out a long sigh. "I have never hidden the truth in my divinations; I always speak plainly. Since I have divined for you, how could I not reveal it? This hexagram not only bears ill omens but also foretells that your very life cannot be preserved. This is your destined end—within three days, on the afternoon of the third night, at precisely the fifth quarter of the *chou* hour, you will depart this world. You will first suffer a headache, then vomit blood and die. Alas, you have served me faithfully for so many years, honest and steadfast in all things. Yet today, I stand by helpless, unable to save you!" As he spoke, tears welled in his eyes.

Ah! Even ants cling to life. Upon hearing Lord Zhou’s words, Peng Jian was so terrified his soul fled to the heavens, his spirit scattered to the nine skies. With a cry of "Ai-yo!" he collapsed to the ground, weeping bitterly. After a long while, he sobbed, "My lord! Is this hexagram truly accurate?"

Lord Zhou replied, "Would I deceive you?"

"You have served me all your life without fault, yet I have never done you any great kindness. Now I give you ten taels of silver—while your destined hour has not yet come, go and enjoy a few cups of wine with gladness! As for all your funeral arrangements, I shall see to them myself. Set your heart at ease and trouble yourself no more about such matters!" With that, he ordered someone to fetch ten taels of silver and handed them to Peng Jian.

But Peng Jian had long known that Lord Zhou’s divine hexagrams were never wrong. Seeing him thus today, he knew the prediction was true. Dropping to his knees, he pleaded, "My lord! Since the hexagram foretells such great misfortune, why not save me?"

Lord Zhou replied, "Life and death are governed by fate—how could I save you? Take the silver and go outside to ease your troubled heart!"

Peng Jian knew well Lord Zhou’s unyielding nature; he understood that further pleas would be futile. Accepting the silver, he left with a heavy heart, head bowed, and tucked the money into his sash. He made his way to a grand tavern, chose a fine seat, and called for the waiter to pour two measures of fine wine and bring several choice dishes. Alone, he poured and drank, lost in thought: *"Today I am still a man, but in three days I will be a ghost. What a wretched fate!"* As the thought weighed on him, tears welled in his eyes.

The tavern staff, who knew Peng Jian well, saw his sorrow and asked, "Master Peng, it’s been ages since you came for a drink. Why the tears today? Has Lord Zhou closed his divination stall, leaving you short of coin?"

Peng Jian replied, "No, it’s not that—I have other troubles on my mind." He drank on in gloom, cup after cup. As the saying goes, *wine enters a sorrowful heart and quickly intoxicates*. Before he had finished the two measures, Peng Jian was thoroughly drunk. Settling his bill, he staggered home, lurching this way and that. Once inside his room, he collapsed fully clothed onto his bed and fell into a deep, snoring sleep that lasted the night.

The next morning, he awoke and immediately thought of his impending doom. Tears streamed down his face as he rose slowly and sat in a chair, muttering to himself, *"Lord Zhou’s divine hexagrams are never wrong, not by the slightest degree. But if a man’s death is fated, how can he escape it? I might as well seek some last pleasures! If only he had told me sooner—I could have had a few more days of joy."* He changed his clothes, left his quarters without reporting to the inner chambers, locked his door, and set off for the streets again.

The servants at the gate had noticed his listless demeanor over the past two days—his comings and goings always with head bowed, silent. They whispered among themselves, unsure of the cause, but dared not ask.

Once outside, Peng Jian headed for another tavern, musing as he walked: *"When Lord Zhou foretold Stone Zongfu’s death, he did not die. Now he says I will die—will I truly die? Or is it a false death? Perhaps even if it’s real, I could feign death like Stone Zongfu."* Then he recalled, *"He said Stone would die in a ruined kiln—if he hadn’t gone out to relieve himself and run outside, he would have been crushed by falling tiles. Since he was crushed, he could escape and live. But I am to die vomiting blood—how can I avoid that?"* Overcome, he wept as he walked.

Lost in grief, he suddenly felt a slap on his shoulder. Startled, he thought the messenger of death had come. *"So soon?"* he cried. Turning, he saw it was a man—upon steadying himself, he recognized Stone Zongfu.

Stone Zongfu had been walking behind and noticed Peng Jian sighing to himself, now looking down, now gazing at the sky, deep in troubled thought. He caught up and tapped his shoulder. "Master Peng, what are you pondering? Why such a gloomy air?" Seeing the tears streaming down his face, he asked, "What on earth is the matter?"

Peng Jian, wiping his tears, replied, "It’s a long story, my good brother. Where are you headed?"

"Home," said Stone.

"Good, we’re going the same way." The two walked together, chatting and laughing along the way.

Then, as if by heaven’s design, Peng Jian suddenly thought, *"Last time, he didn’t die, and Lord Zhou said there must have been a reason. Perhaps he knows a way to avert disaster. Besides, drinking alone is no fun—I’ll buy some wine and food and go to his place. Maybe he can help turn misfortune into fortune!"*

Stopping at a market, he said, "Brother, you’ve just returned home, and we’ve never shared a drink. Since we’re going the same way, let’s buy some wine and dishes. I’ll trouble your wife to prepare them, and we can sit and talk. What do you say?"

With that, he took out some silver and bought wine and dishes. Shi Zongfu tried to stop him but could not, so he let him be. The two carried the food and, in high spirits, arrived at Shi’s doorstep. Shi Zongfu called to open the gate. Old Mrs. Shi, seeing that it was Old Peng, smiled and said, “Master Peng, how have you been? Why have you bought so much food?”

Peng Jian replied, “Sister, as you are an old friend of ours, I wish to share a drink with my brother and speak of some matters.” Old Mrs. Shi took the food inside and went to the kitchen to cook. Peng Jian and Shi Zongfu sat in the hall chatting. But Shi Zongfu noticed that Peng Jian’s words were disjointed, jumping from one thing to another without coherence, and grew suspicious. He thought to himself, *“Could it be that Lord Zhou sent him to pry into the matter? If he’s here to investigate, I must be on guard!”*

Before long, the dishes were ready, and Old Mrs. Shi called her son to bring them out. Peng Jian then invited her to join them at the table. After some polite refusal, they all finally sat down. Peng Jian personally poured the wine and filled the cups, drinking several in a row and sampling a few dishes. Then, unbidden, tears began to stream down his face. Old Mrs. Shi, seeing this, asked in confusion, “Master Peng, what troubles you? Why do you weep while drinking?”

Peng Jian only shook his head in silence. Shi Zongfu smiled and said, “Master Peng, drinking with brothers should be a joyous occasion—why this sorrow? There must be a reason! Are you suffering some injustice at another’s hands?”

Peng Jian replied, “Brother, you wouldn’t understand. I have urgent matters weighing on my heart, and so I weep.”

Old Mrs. Shi pressed, “Master Peng, what *is* the matter? Is it true or false? Why such grief? Won’t you tell us?”

Peng Jian said, “Sister, don’t ask! Today I am a man, but by the fourth watch tomorrow, I will be a ghost—never to see you or your son again!” As he spoke, tears fell like a shuttle’s thread. The mother and son hurriedly asked, “What do you mean?”

Peng Jian then recounted how Lord Zhou had cast his divination, foretelling great misfortune—how he was fated to spit blood and die at the fourth watch that night. He continued, “Sister, Lord Zhou’s divinations are never wrong. I fear my life is truly in peril. That’s why, on the road, I met Brother Shi and thought of how he once escaped death. He must know a way. I beg you and your son to teach me how to avoid this disaster—you would be the saviors of my life!”

At first, Shi Zongfu had suspected Peng Jian was sent by Zhou Qian to inquire about Peach Blossom Girl’s affairs. But now, hearing of the divination and Peng’s certainty of death by the fourth watch, he wept uncontrollably, moved to tears himself. His mother, too, shed tears, reflecting on their own misfortunes and feeling sorrow for another. She said, “Lord Zhou’s divinations are truly accurate. That night in the ruined kiln, if I hadn’t heard my mother’s call and stepped outside, I would have been crushed to death. Now he says you’ll die at the fourth watch tomorrow—it may well come true!”

Peng Jian asked, “Brother, how did you hear your mother’s call in that ruined kiln?” His question left Shi Zongfu speechless, his eyes fixed on Old Peng. Seeing this, Peng Jian knew there was more to the story—and he was not about to let the opportunity slip.

Hastily rising, he bowed deeply to Old Woman Shi and pleaded, "Good mother, have pity and compassion—teach me a way to save my life, and I shall never forget your kindness!" Old Woman Shi replied, "How could there be a way to save a man’s life?"

Seeing her evade the question, Peng Jian immediately knelt before her, saying, "As the old saying goes: *To save a life is better than building a seven-tiered pagoda.*" He kowtowed repeatedly, his forehead striking the ground like a garlic clove being peeled.

Old Woman Shi quickly called her son to help him up, saying, "How could I possibly save a man’s life? My son was saved by someone who gave him a method—otherwise, he would have died in that ruined kiln. He made me swear again and again never to reveal that person’s name, for fear your master Lord Zhou would learn of it and quarrel with him!"

Upon hearing this, Peng Jian suddenly recalled something and asked, "Good mother, was it a *yin* person who taught you that method?" Old Woman Shi was so startled that her face paled.

Whether the Shi mother and son would reveal Miss Ren’s name, and how Old Peng might be saved, will be revealed in the next chapter.

**Chapter Eight**
*Old Woman Shi Reveals the Secret of Salvation; Peach Blossom Girl Leaks the Divine Incantation*

At this, seeing Peng Jian’s desperate pleas and hearing him mention that her son had been saved by a *yin* person, Old Woman Shi was visibly shaken. She asked in alarm, "How did you know it was a *yin* person who saved my son?"

Peng Jian replied, "How would I know? It was only because Lord Zhou once cast a divination, saying that a *yin* person had secretly disrupted his Eight Trigrams, though he could not discern that person’s name. Since you know of such a capable individual, why not tell me? Then I may seek their help. If I, a withered stalk or lingering blade of grass, am granted further life, it will be a great act of hidden merit for you, good mother. I swear I will never reveal their secrets to outsiders."

With that, he prepared to kneel again.

Old Woman Shi, worn down by Peng Jian’s repeated entreaties and recalling how she too had once been in his place for her son’s sake, could not help but be moved. She thought to herself, *"I shall only direct him to seek help from Miss Ren. Whether she aids him or not will be her choice—I will speak vaguely and leave it at that."* Having settled on this course, she said, "Master Peng, I cannot possibly reveal this person’s name. But I will point you toward a path—it will be up to your fate whether you reach them. If you can meet this person, your Five Phases may yet be saved!"

Peng Jian, overjoyed at her words, urged, "Good mother, speak quickly!"

Old Woman Shi replied, "The Ren household next door belongs to the elder and his wife. Do you know them?"

Peng Jian answered, "We are old friends across two generations. In my father’s time, he and Elder Ren were on the best of terms, and even I have often visited them—though it has been a month since my last call. If I go to their home, they will surely insist on hosting me. Every member of their family, young and old, man and woman, I know them all, and they know me."

Old Woman Shi nodded and said, "Since you claim such generational ties with them, all the better! Today you need not go, but tomorrow morning, pay them a visit. When you see Elder Ren, speak of your misfortune—if fate favors you and you meet that capable person, they will surely be able to save you. They possess the power to deliver you. But under no circumstances must you reveal that I directed you to seek their help."

Upon hearing this, Peng Jian lowered his head in thought, then said, "Good mother, your words are somewhat unclear. The Ren household has many members—how am I to know who this capable person is? Whom should I ask for help?"

Shi Zongfu, standing by, curled his lip and said, "Master Peng, you are being rather troublesome! Since you know it is a woman, simply ask among the women of the household. Now, let us drink more!" With that, he poured cup after cup, urging Master Peng to drink several more. Only after securing this lead did Peng Jian’s mind ease slightly, and he drank several cups in succession before taking his leave. Old Woman Shi and her son reiterated their warning, insisting he must not reveal they had sent him. Peng Jian nodded repeatedly in agreement and hurried back to his estate.

The day’s conversation passed swiftly. That night, as he lay in bed—having drunk only a little—he found himself unable to sleep, tossing and turning until the red sun rose in the east. He rose at once, washed his face, changed into fresh clothes, and set off for Elder Ren’s home. Upon arriving at the gate, he informed the doorman, who relayed the message inside. Elder Ren himself came out to greet him, smiling, "Dear nephew, it has been many days since you last visited our humble home. Your arrival this morning is truly a joyous occasion. Why stand on ceremony? There was no need for announcement."

"Who in my household would need to avoid you? Please, come in!" Peng Jian hastily bowed and replied, "It is only proper to observe such courtesy. Though I am as close as family, I must not overstep my bounds." Elder Ren took Peng Jian by the hand and led him to the rear hall, saying along the way, "Old Mistress, our worthy nephew Peng has come."

Now, Elder Ren’s wife had no sons, and her greatest affection was reserved for Peng Jian. As maidservants went inside to announce his arrival, she had already come out to greet him, smiling from a distance, "What fine wind today has blown our worthy nephew here? Why have you not come to see us two old ones for a whole month?" Peng Jian forced a smile and replied, "Aunt, I have been much occupied of late and failed to pay my respects. I trust you are in good health, and that Peach Blossom is well?" The old lady answered, "Quite well."

The two elders invited Peng Jian into the rear chamber, where they had already instructed the servants to prepare a meal. By chance, Peach Blossom had just finished her morning toilette and come to the rear chamber to greet her parents, where she encountered Peng Jian. They exchanged courtesies, and the old lady instructed her daughter to sit beside them. After the maidservants served tea, Elder Ren’s wife said, "Nephew, your uncle and I—and your younger sister—often speak of how you spent more of your childhood in our home than in your own. As you grew, you remained simple and loyal. Yet in the blink of an eye, we two old ones are already over fifty."

Peng Jian replied, "I have always been showered with your kindness, as if we shared the same blood. There is not a day I do not think of coming to pay my respects. Only the burdens of official duties have delayed me." With that, tears began to stream down his face. Elder Ren and his wife assumed he was grieving over their advancing age and quickly consoled him, "Worthy nephew, why such sorrow?"

Peng Jian said, "Seeing you both in your later years, I cannot bear the thought of not being able to attend to you for long." Hearing this, the elderly couple’s hearts grew heavy as well. "Do not speak such inauspicious words," they said. "Though we are old, our bodies remain strong. We may yet share many years together." Peng Jian shook his head, tears flowing, and said, "May you both enjoy long life, but from this day forth, I will no longer be able to see you." With that, he broke into sobs. Startled, Elder Ren and his wife asked, "You are still in the prime of life—why speak such ill-omened words?"

Servants entered bearing trays of dishes. Elder Ren took his seat and said to Peach Blossom Girl, "Daughter, Brother Peng is no outsider—when you were small, he must have held you in his arms countless times. There is no need for you to withdraw today; come, join us for the meal."

Elder Ren and Old Peng sat facing each other, while Madam Ren and her daughter sat side by side at the end of the table. Elder Ren poured wine and passed it to Peng Jian, saying, "Worthy nephew, let your heart be at ease and drink!"

Peng Jian took the cup but set it down, saying, "It is not that I refuse the wine. Today, I came only to see my uncle, aunt, and younger sister—to express my feelings and fulfill my heart’s longing. How could I have the heart to drink?"

Elder Ren said, "Worthy nephew, ever since you entered the door, your face has borne a look of sorrow. First, you spoke of ominous things, and now your words grow even more confused. What, after all, is the matter?"

Peng Jian, tears streaming, replied, "This very night, at the fourth watch, I will die. I came only because I thought of how my uncle and aunt have cared for me, and so I wished to bid you both farewell—for from this day on, you will never see me again!" With that, he broke into loud sobs.

The Ren couple exclaimed in unison, "Where did such words come from?"

"How could a perfectly healthy man die in a single night?" Peng Jian then recounted what Master Zhou had told him from the divination. Elder Ren and his wife said, "So that is the reason. Master Zhou’s hexagrams are not necessarily infallible!"

Just then, Peach Blossom Girl, who had been standing by, saw Peng Jian so distressed—only later did she learn of the divination foretelling his death—could no longer bear it. She called out, "Brother, though my knowledge of divination is but slight, let me try my hand at it. Tell me your birth characters, and I shall calculate for you!" Elder Ren said, "I remember your birth characters as well," and promptly recited Peng Jian’s Eight Characters. Peach Blossom Girl counted on her fingers for a while, then started in surprise. "Master Zhou’s hexagrams were indeed unerring!" She fell into deep thought. The Ren couple hurriedly asked, "Daughter, is Master Zhou’s divination truly accurate?" The young lady replied, "The calculation is flawless. Tonight, at the fourth watch, he will vomit blood and die." The elder couple and Peng Jian all wept, asking, "Is there no way to save him?" Peach Blossom Girl lowered her head in silence. After a long pause, she counted again and said, "There is a way, but it is exceedingly troublesome." Elder Ren and his wife said, "Troublesome or not, we do not mind. For the sake of your parents, save Peng Jian!" The young lady replied, "This method is not to be spoken of lightly. Follow me to the rear garden, and I will tell you." She rose and led Peng Jian to the back garden.

Since the Ren and Peng families were as close as uncle and nephew, the elders paid no heed to the two of them and continued drinking in the rear tower. Peach Blossom Girl and Peng Jian sat down in a small pavilion in the garden. She asked, "Is there a Three Officials Temple within the city?" Peng Jian replied, "There is one, and its incense burns brightly." Peach Blossom Girl said, "I have calculated that tonight, on the fifteenth of the seventh month—the Zhongyuan Festival—the Star Lords of the Northern Dipper will descend to the Jade Capital to record the destinies of mortals. They will return at the second watch and alight at that temple to inscribe the cycles of rebirth. You must prepare a stick of incense, seven cups of pure water, and seven Dipper lamps. Bathe and change your clothes, then set them out in the Three Officials Temple at sunset. With utmost sincerity, recite the sacred name of the Great Sage, the Star Lord of the Northern Dipper, without cease. At the second watch, wait beneath the offering table. I will also give you a treasure pouch." She quickly took a golden bell from a brocade box and handed it to Peng Jian, along with a scroll of the Divine Radiance Incantation. "When the Star Lords descend, do not be afraid. Wait until they call your name, then step out from beneath the table, recite the incantation, and ring the golden bell to petition the Star Lords for longevity. They will surely grant it. This golden bell and incantation are meant to subdue the Star Lords. When you ring and recite, they will be seized with fear and headache. Once the matter is settled, return home and rest. You will be safe. If Master Zhou asks, do not reveal my involvement. This is of the utmost importance! Now go and do as I have instructed."

Peng Jian, upon hearing this, was overjoyed and exclaimed, "Sister, you are my great benefactor! When this matter is settled, I shall return to kowtow in gratitude!" With that, he took his leave. Seeing the two elders, Ren Taigong and his wife, he said, "The method of resolution must not be revealed. I must return home to carry out the instructions!" The two elders, upon hearing this, replied, "In that case, we shall not detain you further!" Ren Taigong then added, "If all goes well, you must come by tomorrow morning, Nephew, so that we two elders need not worry!" Peng Jian readily agreed, "That is only natural."

That evening, Peng Jian purified his body and, following the young lady’s instructions, completed every step. He had servants carry him to the Three Officials Temple and instructed the temple keeper, "No one is to enter tonight!" Alone, he knelt in the center, recited the sacred titles of the Northern Dipper Star Lords, and burned incense. As the second watch arrived, he heard a gust of wind—just as the appointed hour drew near—so he quickly concealed himself beneath the offering table. A waft of extraordinary fragrance filled the air, and voices spoke: "Whose offering is this? How did they know we Star Lords would descend? They have prepared so immaculately."

After a brief pause, he suddenly heard voices calling names from below, each one distinctly audible. Then came a sudden call: **"Peng Jian!"** A voice from the altar responded: **"Fated to live fifty years. Tonight, at the fourth watch, he shall die coughing blood!"** Peng Jian, hearing this, was struck with terror, his soul trembling in fear.

*How Peng Jian’s fate unfolds this night shall be revealed in the next chapter.*

**Chapter Nine, Volume Three**
*Peng Jian Seeks Salvation to Extend His Lifespan*
*Zhou Qian, Enraged, Smashes a Divination*
*A poem reads:*
*Why do I dwell in these emerald mountains?*
*I smile but say nothing, my heart at ease.*
*Peach blossoms drift on flowing waters, gone without trace—*
*Another realm lies beyond, not of this mortal world.*

Now, Peng Jian, crouched beneath the offering table, heard a deity call his name and declare, **"Tonight, at the fourth watch, he is destined to die coughing blood."** Terrified, he hastily recited incantations, striking his golden chime. Then he heard the Fire Virtue Star Lord demand: **"Who dares use spells to oppose us?"** Peng Jian poked his head out from under the table and saw nine august deities seated on either side, each of strange and fearsome appearance. He immediately prostrated himself in the center, ceaselessly reciting incantations and striking the golden chime.

The first Star Lord spoke: **"Peng Jian! Cease your noise and stop chanting! Do you seek extended life? Then plead before the fifth Star Lord."** The fifth Star Lord then declared: **"We have accepted his offerings, and he is a man of loyalty and kindness, free of wicked deeds. Moreover, the Peach Orchard Immortal instructed him to seek our aid, that we might alter his destined encounter with demonic forces. We shall now change his name and grant him added years—a sign that good is rewarded with good!"** He called out: **"Peng Jian! Come forward. We shall bestow upon you a new name: henceforth, you shall be called Peng Zu. We grant you a lifespan of one hundred years. The Left and Right Assistant Star Lords each grant you fifty years, and every Star Lord here grants you one hundred years—altogether, eight hundred and fifty years! On the third and twenty-seventh days of each month, you must fast, bathe, and reverently worship the Dipper. Do not reveal heavenly secrets, lest you incur divine punishment!"**

Peng Jian kowtowed and replied: **"This humble one, Peng Jian, having received the sacred gift of a new name and extended life, fears that living such a great span without wealth or descendants would only bring suffering. I beg the august deities to bestow some measure of prosperity, that I may live out my days in comfort!"** The Star Lords agreed: **"That is reasonable."** One deity drew a pill from his robe and instructed Peng Jian to swallow it, saying: **"This elixir will transform your bones and renew your body, rendering you free of all illness—so that you may enjoy the three blessings of fortune, emolument, and longevity!"** Then two of the deities each produced a ledger, and though Peng Jian could not see how they inscribed them, they finished writing and vanished in a gust of pure wind.

At that moment, Peng Jian felt his spirit invigorated a hundredfold, his heart brimming with joy. **Gentlemen, this is the very Peng Zu who lived over eight hundred years among men, taking thirteen wives—a man who enjoyed great fortune and longevity!** Truly:
*Without the golden elixir, even a century of life is hard to attain.*

This night had already passed the fourth watch when Peng Jian thought to himself: *"Miss Ren instructed me that once my task was complete, I should return to the mansion to rest. I understand her intent—she feared that if Lord Zhou saw I had not died and had spent the night away, he would surely grow suspicious and demand an explanation. Why not follow Miss Ren’s advice and hurry back to the mansion?"* With that resolved, he roused the temple warden, had the gates opened, and rushed back to the estate. Silently, he called for the main gate to be unbarred, entered his chamber, and collapsed onto his bed to sleep.

Meanwhile, Zhou Qian had sat alone until the fifth watch, convinced Peng Jian was dead. He took up the Heavenly Stem Sword, woke his page to carry a lantern, and personally went to Peng Jian’s room. Pushing open the door and stepping to the bedside, he saw Peng Jian lying motionless, face upturned, eyes half-closed. Believing him dead, he could not help but sigh in grief: *"Alas! A man of such lifelong integrity—now utterly gone!"* Hurriedly, he removed his golden crown, unbound his hair, and brandished his sword as he paced the Dipper steps, chanting incantations in an attempt to bind Peng Jian’s three *hun* and six *po* souls, preventing their dispersal. Only then did he intend to perform rites to guide him toward a favorable rebirth.

Unexpectedly, Peng Jian awoke with a start. Opening his eyes, he saw Lord Zhou with disheveled hair and sword in hand, pacing and chanting. With a grunt, he sat up—startling Zhou Qian so badly that the latter leapt back, sword raised, and barked: *"Vile ghost, cease your haunting! By the authority of the Most High Lord Lao, I command you—begone!"*

Peng Jian could not suppress a laugh. *"My lord, what rites are you performing?"*

Zhou Qian steadied his spirit and demanded: *"Peng Jian! Are you man or ghost?"*

*"I am a man—I never died. How could I be a ghost?"*

Zhou Qian then ordered his page to raise the lantern for a closer look. *"Strange, most strange! Who taught you the remedy to return from the brink of death? Speak at once!"*

Peng Jian replied, *"To die when fated not to die is to live a few years more. Why does my lord grow so anxious? Must I die for your wishes to be fulfilled?"*

Lord Zhou, displeased by these words, seethed inwardly: *"This wretch dares prevaricate to my face! I shall lure him to the study and interrogate him thoroughly—he must reveal who taught him the method to break my Eight Trigrams!"* Resolving this, he summoned Peng Jian: *"Follow me to the study!"*

Peng Jian dared not refuse and trailed after Lord Zhou, thinking to himself: *"He will surely press me for the truth. Even if I die, I shall never utter Miss Ren’s name!"* Before he knew it, they had arrived at the study.

Lord Zhou took his seat in the center, adjusted his topknot and cap, and set down the Heavenly Stem Sword. He then ordered his page: *"Summon several men to enter!"* Soon after, several servants filed in. Lord Zhou barked: *"Bind Peng Jian for me!"*

The servants dared not disobey and swiftly fetched ropes to bind Peng Jian. Peng Jian cried out: *"Peng Jian is innocent!"*

Lord Zhou, enraged, glared at him: *"You deceive me—how can you be innocent? Confess at once who devised the means to save you, or I shall have you put to death this very moment!"*

Hearing this, Peng Jian hastily knelt and pleaded: *"I am but a fool—what power do I possess? I had resolved to die that night, yet somehow slept through it and awoke alive—how, I cannot say!"*

Before he could finish, Lord Zhou roared: *"Bah! Lies, all of it! You will not speak the truth unless beaten!"*

The attendants were ordered: *"Give him one hundred lashes first!"* Two servants immediately fetched two leather whips, stepped before Peng Jian, and set to work—truly delivering a hundred strokes. The beating left Peng Jian sprawled upon the ground, wailing in agony.

Now, those in official households all claim the yamen’s impartiality, but how could it be so? These servants, moreover, had always been on good terms with Peng Jian—who among them would heartlessly flog him a full hundred times? In truth, no more than twenty or thirty lashes struck home. Thus, Peng Jian suffered little harm, crying out all the while: *"My lord wrongs me with this beating! I miscalculated the yin and yang myself—what fault lies with another?"*

Lord Zhou flew into a rage: *"You’ve always been honest—today you dare lie to me! Very well, I’ll not beat you further. Attendants, bind him with another rope around his waist and hoist him up beneath the eaves!"*

By now, Peng Jian felt the pain keenly, yet mindful of Peach Blossom Girl’s lifesaving kindness—the earnest instructions she had given him the night before, warning him never to reveal her name—he gritted his teeth and said nothing.

Lord Zhou strode down the steps and pressed him: *"Speak the truth at once, and not only will I spare you punishment, I shall reward you handsomely. I see your face aglow with crimson light, your lifespan extended—you must have met some extraordinary person who taught you the art of bone-transformation and rebirth. Tell me everything!"*

Hearing this, Peng Jian’s heart lurched: *"How sharp his insight! Not only are his divinations accurate, but his physiognomy is flawless as well. Since I cannot deny it, I’ll say nothing at all and see how he questions me further."* With that, he squeezed his eyes shut and sealed his lips.

Upon seeing this, Lord Zhou’s fury blazed. He turned and strode back to the main hall, seized the Heavenly Stem Sword, and rushed before Peng Jian, roaring: *"Peng Jian! If you refuse to speak, you commit the crime of deceiving your lord!"* With that, he raised the sword in a vicious arc, poised to strike.

Peng Jian’s eyes flew open—his soul scattered in terror. *"Spare me, my lord!"* he shrieked. *"I’ll tell you everything!"*

Lord Zhou snarled: *"If you delay another instant, I’ll cleave you in two!"*

Hastily, Peng Jian blurted: *"It was Ren Taogong’s daughter, Ren Taohua—neighbor to Shi Zongfu on the left—who instructed me. Last night at the third watch, she told me to go to the Three Officials Temple and await the arrival of the Star Lord of the Northern Dipper to beg for longevity. That is how I survived."*

Hearing this, Lord Zhou ordered Peng Jian released. He returned to the central hall, seated himself, and demanded: *"Peng Jian! Why did you not speak sooner?"*

Peng Jian bowed in apology, then added: *"Miss Taohua repeatedly warned me never to tell you, my lord, fearing you would grow angry and bear a grudge against her. Even Shi Zongfu was taught by her."*

At these words, Lord Zhou could not suppress his rage.

*"Wretched schemer! First she shattered my Eight Trigrams formation—let that pass—but now she sends the Shi mother and son to humiliate me. I swear I shall not rest until I’ve settled this!"*

Peng Jian, hearing this, hastily kowtowed: *"My lord, I beg you not to bear a grudge against this lowly one! If you do, it will only implicate me in her misdeeds. Have mercy, my lord—her parents have but this one daughter, and she is still so young."*

Lord Zhou asked: *"How old is this wretched girl?"*

*"She has just turned sixteen this year,"* Peng Jian replied.

The chronicler adds: Though Peach Blossom and Lord Zhou descended to the mortal realm one after the other, why is Lord Zhou so much older? Because in heaven, a single moment spans many years on earth. Lord Zhou arrived but an hour or two before Peach Blossom, and thus is decades her senior.

But enough digression. When Lord Zhou heard Peng Jian’s truthful account, he rewarded him with ten taels of silver to tend his wounds. Peng Jian expressed his gratitude, and Lord Zhou warned him: *"You are forbidden to breathe a word of this to the Ren household. If I learn you have spoken of it, your punishment will be doubled!"*

*"I dare not! I dare not!"* Peng Jian replied, bowing repeatedly before retiring to his quarters.

Lord Zhou pondered in secret: *"Peach Blossom is but a child—how could she possess such mastery of the Dao? I find it hard to believe. I must verify whether the Northern Dipper truly descended last night."* He swiftly calculated the hour and confirmed: indeed, at the first quarter of the third watch, the Northern Dipper had descended upon the Three Officials Temple east of the city. His heart filled with dread: *"Peach Blossom’s arts truly commune with the divine! With her in Zhaoge, I fear I shall never escape her influence."* He paced the flower tower, lost in thought, until a sudden inspiration struck: *"Why not... thus and thus... to erase this grudge from my heart!"* Resolved, he summoned a servant named Xu Cheng and commanded: *"Fetch the official matchmaker at once."*

Xu Cheng departed, and Lord Zhou waited. What scheme he devised to harm Peach Blossom, read in the next chapter.

---

**Chapter Ten: A Deceitful Betrothal—Coercion and Trickery Seal Her Doom**

Lord Zhou ordered his servant Xu Cheng to summon the official matchmaker. Before long, Xu returned with a woman surnamed Jiang. Seeing the hall crowded, Lord Zhou dismissed all attendants, seated himself in the center, and beckoned the matchmaker forward. She kowtowed, and he smiled as he spoke: *"Matchmaker, do you know the Ren household south of the city? They have a daughter called Peach Blossom. Do you know her? Have you ever seen her?"*

The matchmaker replied: *"I know the Ren matriarch—her family is wealthy, with tens of thousands in assets, and they are upright folk. As for Miss Peach Blossom, I have never laid eyes on her, so I dare not speak idly. From what I gather, she must be sixteen or seventeen."*

Lord Zhou said: *"I have heard this young lady is of refined appearance, and I wish to betroth her as my daughter-in-law. If you succeed in arranging this, I shall reward you handsomely!"*

The matchmaker hesitated, thinking: *"I have never heard of Lord Zhou having a son. This request is most peculiar!"* Seeing her reluctance, Lord Zhou grew displeased and pressed: *"Why do you remain silent?"*

She replied: *"It is not that I refuse to speak. I only wonder—how could a commoner like Ren Taogong dare to ally with Your Lordship?"*

Lord Zhou said: *"You need only go and propose it. I wish to take her as my daughter-in-law, and the wedding must be held within three days. They need not provide a single dowry item."*

Before he could finish, the matchmaker interrupted: *"This is impossible! Who ever heard of a bride entering her husband’s home in three days? The deadline is far too tight—it would only send me on a fool’s errand. I suspect Your Lordship has some ulterior motive. Why not confide in me? Whatever happens, if the Rens raise objections, you can intervene. What harm could there be?"*

Hearing this, Lord Zhou’s anger turned to delight: *"You are indeed clever. I shall tell you the truth—I intend to punish Peach Blossom for shattering my Eight Trigrams formation. I have no son; this is merely a ruse to lure her here so I may kill her. The third day hence is an inauspicious day when malevolent spirits descend, so I have set the date. The moment she steps from her palanquin, her life will be forfeit. This is a secret method to dispose of her—you, as the matchmaker, bear no responsibility. If you succeed, I shall reward you with a hundred taels of gold, and I shall not go back on my word."*

"Ah, so that is the reason!" exclaimed Matchmaker Jiang. "No wonder Your Lordship was so enraged. But Peach Blossom is merely a sheltered maiden—how could she have disrupted Your Lordship’s Eight Trigrams formation? If she can be secretly done away with, leaving no trace, I am more than willing to make the journey. Only, we must devise a scheme to trick Old Master Ren into agreeing."

Pleased that Matchmaker Jiang’s words aligned with his own, Lord Zhou’s heart swelled with delight. "Not difficult at all," he said. "Let me first calculate the omens to see how it should be done." He swiftly counted on his fingers, then declared, "The ruse for the betrothal is set! I’ve just divined that Old Master Ren is not at home—he has gone to his estate and will return tomorrow at the Hour of Si. I shall send Xu Cheng with you to wait at his gate. You must do exactly as I say: if he complies, all is well; if he refuses, tell him I will report his daughter to the authorities for using sorcery and unholy arts to shatter my Eight Trigrams formation. He will have no choice but to agree!"

Matchmaker Jiang, overjoyed at the plan, replied, "This scheme is brilliant! I shall go tomorrow."

Lord Zhou was overjoyed and rewarded Matchmaker Jiang with wine and food, then presented her with twenty taels of silver. Matchmaker Jiang, ecstatic, bowed in gratitude and returned home.

The next day, she met Xu Cheng as arranged, and together they left the estate. Along the way, they finalized their plan and proceeded straight to the Ren residence. Just as they arrived, it was the Hour of Si, and Old Master Ren appeared from the distance. The two exchanged delighted glances, murmuring, "The Duke’s divination is truly divine!" As they thought this, Old Master Ren reached his gate and dismounted. A servant carried a bundle of clothes behind him.

Seeing Matchmaker Jiang and another man waiting at his doorstep, Old Master Ren smiled and said, "Madam Jiang, why do you not come inside to sit? What brings you to stand at my gate?" Matchmaker Jiang greeted him with a cheerful face and replied, "Master Ren, see what I have in this basket? Yesterday was the day my daughter served tea to her betrothed, and I must deliver gifts to all the families involved. Here are some tea cakes for you and the mistress of the house. Since you’ve just returned, perhaps your young servant could take them inside for you." With that, she handed the basket to the attendant following Master Ren.

Old Master Ren said, "So your daughter has set a wedding date—how wonderful! Please, come inside for some tea."

Matchmaker Jiang promptly assented and, together with Old Master Ren and Xu Cheng, entered the main hall to take their seats. She then retrieved the basket from the young servant’s hands and presented it to Master Ren, saying, “Master Ren, pray take a look—it’s nothing much, just a small token of respect.” Old Master Ren repeatedly demurred, “You honor me too much,” before accepting the basket. Upon lifting the lid, he saw a piece of red silk covering the contents, adorned with a pair of golden floral hairpins. He reached in, removed them, and set them on the table, revealing a dozen or so delicate pastries nestled within.

Matchmaker Jiang, ever the eager hostess, urged from the side, “Master Ren, do try one!” Now, Old Master Ren had come straight from the countryside without having eaten, and his stomach was indeed empty. Moreover, the pastries looked exquisite, and the old man, fond of sweets as elders often are, found himself unable to resist—especially with Matchmaker Jiang pressing him so. Without thinking, he plucked one and placed it in his mouth.

Just then, the young servant brought out tea. Old Master Ren offered it to his guests while pouring himself a cup, savoring the pastries slowly as he sipped. “What fine pastries!” he remarked. “Truly, their fragrance fills the mouth.”

Matchmaker Jiang, feigning playfulness, took up the pair of golden hairpins and stepped forward to pin them on Old Master Ren’s head, laughing, “How delightful! How delightful! Today we take this as an auspicious sign—let me find you a fine concubine tomorrow, Master Ren, so you may yet sire a son!” Old Master Ren, taking it as mere jest, replied with a chuckle, “That would be quite impossible.”

Xu Cheng, seizing the red silk, draped it over Old Master Ren’s shoulders. Then, both he and Matchmaker Jiang knelt in unison and kowtowed, exclaiming, “Congratulations, Master Ren! Felicitations, Master Ren!”

Startled, Old Master Ren quickly asked, “Why do you both jest so?” and reached out to help them rise.

The two rose and said, “Let us speak plainly! This was sent by Duke Zhou for Master Ren. His son wishes to marry your daughter, and he too is sixteen this year. Only, the matter is urgent, and we feared you might refuse, so we devised this ruse to deceive you. Pray, do not take offense!”

Old Master Ren, now realizing it was a betrothal trick, grew furious and said, “Marriage is a weighty affair—both families must consent. Does he rely on his ducal power to bully common folk? Do I fear him so much that I dare not speak, and must yield to him? I shall *not* agree to this match, and let him do his worst!”

Matchmaker Jiang replied, “Master Ren, do not be angered. This is his servant, whom I brought along. I told him you might refuse. The Duke said, ‘No matter. If he refuses, I shall accuse him in court of using sorcery and black magic to disrupt my Eight Trigrams!’ Consider—every official in Chaoge City is on good terms with him. You may yet come to harm!”

Old Master Ren, upon hearing this, remained silent and mused to himself, *"I regret letting my daughter meddle in others’ affairs. If I refuse now, he will take me to court, and I shall surely suffer. Besides, I have already eaten his betrothal cakes."* He then thought, *"A daughter must marry someday. To be matched with the Duke of Zhou’s son—what an honor!"* Turning to the two, he said, “Gentlemen, is it not a fine thing for this old man to be allied with the Duke? Yet there is still the disparity in status, and I have not even met the young master. Moreover, the wedding date is too soon.”

Matchmaker Jiang smiled and replied, “For the Duke to ally with you, Master Ren, is to become one family. Besides, his household took the initiative in seeking this match. His son, raised in luxury, must surely be handsome. The only issue is the haste of the date. The Duke has already considered this and instructed us to say, ‘If Master Ren finds the date too soon, he may forgo all dowry—only the young lady need come as she is.’”

Hearing this, Old Master Ren’s heart filled with joy. “If that is the case, I must still discuss it with my wife. I cannot decide alone.” Matchmaker Jiang said, “The husband is the head of the household. If you consent, your wife will surely agree. We shall now return to report the good news to the Duke—that you have given your blessing!” Xu Cheng nodded in understanding, and the two departed.

Left alone, Old Master Ren sat in the main hall in a daze, turning the matter over in his mind. A smile crept upon his face as he thought of the honor of such a high match, forgetting all else. He rose, beaming, and made his way inside. When Mistress Ren saw him enter with such cheer, she stood and said, “Master, you’re back!” Noticing the golden flowers in his hair and the red silk draped over his shoulder, she could not help but laugh. “Master, what’s the occasion? Are you officiating a wedding today, or have you taken a concubine, decked in flowers and silk, to bow before heaven and earth?”

Old Master Ren chuckled. “Neither, my dear. I bring good news—for both of us!” He sat down and recounted in detail the Duke’s proposal. “You once said our daughter bore the marks of nobility. Now it has come to pass! We old folk shall bask in her glory!”

Mistress Ren, delighted, replied, “For a common family to wed into nobility—what honor! But to send her without any dowry would be improper.” Old Master Ren smiled. “What need have we for dowry? Everything she wears and uses is new. We can prepare the rest in three days and send it to the Zhou estate—it will not be late. There is only one thing: I wonder if our daughter will be pleased. Let us go and speak with her.”

Mistress Ren, finding Old Master Ren’s words reasonable, accompanied him to the rear garden. There they saw Peach Blossom Girl alone, carrying a flower pot, watering a peach tree. The two elders called out together, “Daughter, why trouble yourself to water the tree? Let the maidservants do it.” Seeing her parents enter, Peach Blossom Girl quickly set down the pot, and they all ascended the flower pavilion to sit.

Noticing her father adorned with flowers and draped in red, Peach Blossom Girl smiled and asked, “What joyous occasion has made you don these today, Father and Mother?” Mistress Ren spoke first: “The happiness of us two elders is all thanks to you, my child.” She then recounted in full how “the Duke of Zhou had sent a matchmaker to propose marriage, and your father has already agreed to your departure on the nineteenth.”

Before she could finish, Peach Blossom Girl’s face turned ashen yellow. With a cry of “Oh no!” her body collapsed helplessly from the chair to the ground.

Whether Peach Blossom Girl’s life would be spared, or if she would consent to the marriage—these matters shall be revealed in the next chapter.

---

**Chapter Eleven**
*Resenting the Marriage, Demanding Betrothal Gifts*
*Invoking Malevolent Forces, Poisoning with Schemes*

The moment Peach Blossom Girl heard her parents had promised her in marriage to the Zhou family, she could not bear to listen further. Overcome with fury, she writhed in her seat before collapsing to the floor.

Just as:
*A tender blossom, drenched by rain, wilts powerless,*
*A slender willow, buffeted by wind, bends beyond endurance.*

Seeing their daughter sprawled upon the ground, Old Master Ren and his wife were struck with terror, their souls scattering like lost spirits. They rushed forward together, lifting her up, crying, “Our precious child! What ails you so?”—and burst into tears.

Peach Blossom Girl, once seated again, brooded in silence before speaking: “Father, Mother—how could you act so rashly, falling into another’s snare? This is all Lord Zhou’s scheme, and now we have walked straight into his trap! I have learned that Lord Zhou has no son at all, and his wife passed away long ago. He has only a daughter, who is already sixteen this year. Now he insists on marrying me at once and demands I enter his household within three days. I am certain this is all because of Brother Peng’s affair. Seeing how I shattered his Eight Trigrams, shame turned to fury, and now he seeks this marriage only to use his arts to kill me. I fear this may be the last time I see you both—we may never meet again!”

Old Master Ren and his wife, hearing these words, were struck dumb with terror. “Why speak such ill omens when all was well?” they stammered.

Peach Blossom Girl, no ordinary mortal, foresaw events as clearly as if they had already come to pass. She hastily calculated on her fingers and saw through the hidden truth: “The nineteenth day is when the Malevolent Spirit descends—a day of great misfortune. Lord Zhou has chosen this day to strike me dead!”

Old Master Ren’s fury erupted. “Lord Zhou is truly despicable! How dare he plot such harm!”

“I’ll not spare this old life of mine—I’ll fight him to the death! We’ll take this to the magistrate; I fear him not!” With that, he tore the red-and-green betrothal headdress from his head, crumpled it to shreds, and stamped it underfoot.

Peach Blossom Girl thought to herself, “Since I was sent down by the Jade Decree to break Lord Zhou’s arts, I cannot escape my fate. Better to set my parents’ minds at ease and spare them this distress.” She said, “Father, Mother, put your hearts at rest! This is Heaven’s decree—I do not fear him! Yet after raising me all these years, I have repaid you nothing; I have failed in my great debt to you.”

Old Master Ren and his wife, hearing this, wept tears of pearl. “How can we consent to this inauspicious, baleful day?” they cried.

Peach Blossom Girl replied, “To others, this day would bring harm, but I can break its curse. If others could be saved from it, how could I not save myself? Do not worry, Father and Mother—I do not fear it! I shall return within three days. Tell them I require Lord Zhou to provide me with several things, and then we may proceed with the chosen day.”

Old Master Ren, overjoyed, asked, “What does he need to prepare? I’ll send the matchmaker to fetch it at once.”

Peach Blossom Girl said, “Nothing extraordinary. I require two feet of red silk, embroidered with the Eight Immortals of the Grotto-Heavens on the bridal sedan. The sedan must be adorned with multicolored silks, and a pair of empty treasure vases, filled with the Five Grains and an iron. When the sedan arrives at our gate, burn sandalwood and cypress leaves in the vases and iron, and have one of his household carry the iron, circling the sedan three times before I enter. Only then may the sedan pass through the gates. At both the outer and inner gates, place a horse saddle and a square peck measure. The bride must step over the saddle after alighting from the sedan before bowing to Heaven and Earth. From his main gate to the inner hall, he must lay out a carpet of colored felts so that the bride’s feet never touch the ground. He must also send his tailor to await our instructions. If Lord Zhou refuses even one of these requests, I shall not marry into his household. Moreover, his son must come to marry in—he must enter our family as a son-in-law. Father, see to it that all is prepared without delay or error!”

Old Master Ren committed every word to memory, then took up the Four Treasures of the Study and listed each item on paper, ensuring not a single one was omitted. Knowing their daughter possessed such skill and feared not Lord Zhou, the couple cast aside their worries and rejoiced. “Daughter,” they said, “since you can break his arts, we are at ease. When the matchmaker arrives, we shall have her request these things from Lord Zhou.”

The two elders left the garden in high spirits, while Peach Blossom Girl remained behind, making preparations to counter Lord Zhou’s arts.

Meanwhile, the matchmaker Jiang and Xu Cheng returned to the estate and reported to Lord Zhou, “Old Master Ren has agreed to the marriage, with the bride to be fetched on the nineteenth.”

Lord Zhou was overjoyed. He rewarded the matchmaker with silver and Xu Cheng with ten taels of white silver. Fearing the Rens might change their minds, he instructed Jiang and Xu to prepare the betrothal gifts and wine boxes at once, along with several maidservants from his household. Laden with sheep and wine, they set off to present the gifts at the Ren residence.

Upon arrival, Old Master Ren had his servants entertain the guests in the main hall while the women were ushered into the inner chambers. Without inspecting the gifts, he ordered them taken directly to the great kitchen. The matchmaker and the maidservants entered the inner room, kowtowed, and offered their congratulations. Old Mistress Ren then said, “Matchmaker Jiang, how could you be so careless? I am not angry about the deception in this marriage, but why choose the nineteenth—a day of great misfortune? Lord Zhou is a man of reason; why did he not check the almanac and instead try to deceive me with this paper coffin? I shall not pursue the matter further. But go back and tell Lord Zhou this: prepare all the items for the bridal procession. If even one is missing, do not blame us for breaking our word. Let him take us to court—I am willing to face the magistrate!”

The matchmaker bowed and replied, “Old Mistress, please calm your anger! If the items are impossible to find, then perhaps they do not exist. But if they can be found, I guarantee Lord Zhou will provide them all without fail.”

Old Master Ren said, “They are not impossible to find—just everyday objects. Here is a red list with everything written clearly. Take it back to Lord Zhou and have him send them as specified.” He handed over the red paper.

The matchmaker, unable to read, asked, “Master Ren, please read it aloud so I know what these items are.”

Old Master Ren recited the list. The matchmaker laughed and said, “I thought they were things rare as phoenix feathers or unicorn horns! These are simple enough—no trouble at all! Leave it to me; not a single item will be missing!”

“Old Master Ren said, ‘Pray inform Lord Zhou that the items requested today were divined by a yin-yang master, who declared the day most inauspicious. These objects may avert the omen—otherwise, my daughter will surely perish. Hence my persistence. Though I am but a commoner, I would not renege on my word to break the betrothal. Lord Zhou, as a nobleman of high rank, must not begrudge fulfilling this request. You may all return now!’

The matchmaker assented repeatedly, then hastily took leave of Old Master Ren with her companions and rushed back to the manor. Upon seeing Lord Zhou, she exclaimed, ‘The Ren household is most formidable! It is as if they have a divine informant—every detail of Your Lordship’s affairs seems foreknown!’ She then presented the red list of requested items.

Lord Zhou took it and glanced over it. ‘This is no difficulty,’ he said. ‘I shall comply with every demand. Go quickly and inform them that I shall provide all as specified. When the time comes, have Peng Jian deliver them, and let them be used as they see fit.’

The matchmaker, having heard this, returned to Old Master Ren’s residence to relay the message.

Now, Lord Zhou’s *Tian Gang Divine Manual* contained only methods of divination, not means of countering omens. Thus, he had taken the items requested by Peach Blossom Girl lightly, paying them no further mind.

On the evening of the eighteenth, Lord Zhou sat alone in his study, calculating the positions of the inauspicious spirits’ descent. He discerned that the Four Absolutes and Four Annihilations lay in the northeast, the Wailing Spirit in the north, the Heavenly Net and Earthly Snare in the east, while the Dipper-Wood Beast, Ghost-Metal Ram, Mao-Day Hare, and Star-Sun Horse converged in the northeast corner. Greatly pleased, he declared, ‘The gathering of these malevolent forces aligns perfectly with the direction of my chamber—no need to summon them. Were it another, a single countermeasure would suffice to claim their life.’”

Lord Zhou mused, “Peach Blossom Girl must possess some skill—else why would she demand so many items? What if these are not mere trifles but the very means of countering my scheme? Should she outmaneuver me and escape this calamity, her prowess would be proven, and what face would I have left? Better to make this a case of ‘an open spear is easily dodged, but a hidden arrow is hard to guard against.’ Since she cannot possibly calculate the descent of these malevolent spirits, why not secretly summon a few more baleful deities to lie in wait at every direction? The moment her bridal palanquin passes, whichever fiend she encounters shall claim that wretched harlot’s life! Even if she wields some sorcery, she will have no time to counter them all!”

Having settled on his plan, he hastened to bathe and change his robes. Tucking the *Celestial Stem Divine Manual* into his breast, he grasped the Celestial Stem Sword and entered the rear garden. There, he instructed his attendants to prepare a table laden with incense, flowers, lamps, candles, fresh brush and ink, and yellow paper, then ordered all servants to withdraw and forbade them from peering inside. He barred the door and waited until the third watch of the night.

At last, Lord Zhou approached the table, removed his golden crown, and unbound his hair. Drawing forth the *Celestial Stem Divine Manual*, he copied its talismanic seals onto yellow paper with cinnabar ink. Holding the sword in his left hand, he burned the talisman with his right, recited the incantation, and pointed the Celestial Stem Sword skyward. A gust of eerie wind arose, and as it subsided, a wisp of smoky cloud descended, bearing a celestial general of fearsome aspect:

A golden helm bristling with baleful qi,
A face black as ink, brows thick as brushstrokes,
Eyes like lanterns upon Mount Ao,
A beard stiff as needles,
A bamboo-node steel whip gripped in hand—
By Heaven’s decree, he was named the Great Marshal,
And the two characters “Black Fiend” struck terror into gods and ghosts alike!

With a thunderous sound, the deity materialized before the table, bowing deeply. “For what purpose does the ritual master summon this spirit?”

Lord Zhou swiftly closed his eyes and replied, “I would not dare disturb your eminence without cause. Tomorrow at the Hour of Si, Peach Blossom Girl will wed. I humbly beseech your aid: go to Elder Ren’s home and await her. When she boards her palanquin, strike her dead within it with your steel whip, then return to your post.”

The deity assented, “I obey the ritual command!”—and vanished in an instant.

Lord Zhou then burned a second talisman. With equal swiftness, a figure descended from the heavens: disheveled hair, clad in mourning garb, a yellow porcelain urn in the right hand and a funeral staff in the left. This was the Funeral Gate Deity, overseer of mortal deaths. Seeing the god’s overwhelming presence, Lord Zhou again closed his eyes.

The deity bowed and asked, “What task does the ritual master assign?”

“Forgive my presumption,” Lord Zhou said. “Tomorrow at the Hour of Si, Peach Blossom Girl’s bridal palanquin will arrive. I beg your eminence to wait at the left of the gate. Should she step from the palanquin, strike her dead with your divine might, then return to your post.”

The deity replied, “I accept the ritual command!”—and vanished in a gust of wind.

Lord Zhou hastily burned a third talisman, summoning the Hanging Guest Deity, whom he stationed at the right of the gate, charging him to strike Peach Blossom Girl dead before returning to his post.

As for the fourth talisman and the deity it summoned—what mighty spirit would descend? That shall be revealed in the next chapter.

**Chapter Twelve**
*Overt Snares and Hidden Escapes*
*Foreshadowing the Future’s Secrets*

The White Tiger Deity stood a full *zhang* in golden stature, his painted halberd held aloft in hand. His silver helm gleamed with the aura of life and death, his armor clad in scales like dragon’s mail. A belt of polished jade and precious gems girded his waist, while his five-colored battle boots stirred auspicious clouds. His face was powdered pale, his brows sharp as drawn blades, his eyes flashing fourfold—terrifying to behold!

When asked his name and title, he declared: “I am the White Tiger Deity, mightily ruling the four directions.”

The White Tiger Deity approached the altar and asked, “What command does the ritual master have for me?”

Lord Zhou replied, “I would not dare trouble you without cause. Tomorrow at the Hour of Si, the bridal procession for Ren Taohua will arrive. I humbly beseech your divine power to manifest your might: when she enters the bridal chamber for the *zuo zhang* ritual, devour this woman to death—only then may you return to your post.”

The White Tiger Deity received the talismanic decree and vanished in a shimmering ascent into the sky. Thus, Lord Zhou had summoned all four principal deities. He put away the *Book of Heavenly Stem Divinities*, smoothed his hair, and ordered the attendants to clear the altar offerings. Returning to his chambers, he rejoiced inwardly.

“Ren Taohua!” he mused. “Even if you possess the power to reverse heaven’s will, you cannot escape this calamity! Though I have summoned these four mighty deities with the darkest malice to harm you, this is a disaster of your own making!”

After some reflection, as the fourth watch of the night approached, he finally retired to sleep. The night passed without incident.

Meanwhile, Ren Taohua, determined to prove her superiority over Lord Zhou, had already prepared all her treasures. The next morning, after completing her toilette, she hurried to the rear garden to water her peach tree, only to feel a sudden unease. She quickly calculated the hidden patterns of yin and yang, then could not help but chuckle to herself. “Lord Zhou!” she murmured. “You still underestimate me. Now you’ve summoned four malevolent deities to secretly harm me—what a futile effort! How could you ever succeed?”

She rushed back to her embroidered chamber, opened a brocade pouch, and took out a small peach branch. Carrying it to the rear garden, she began to chant under her breath. With a breath of qi, she blew upon the branch and commanded, *“Swift as thought, return to true form!”* In an instant, the branch elongated, transforming into a seven-foot halberd, its blade gleaming like a painted halberd. She grasped it in hand, unbound her raven tresses, and let them cascade over her powdered face. With one hand forming a mudra and the other raising the halberd, she recited an incantation and cried, *“Red Calamity Deity, descend at once!”*

Ren Taohua’s foundational Daoist arts surpassed Lord Zhou’s. Having cultivated for years in the Jasper Pool and possessing a celestial tome bestowed by Qi Zhenren—the foremost among all divine sages—her invocation was the *Qi Zhenren’s Summoning Spell*. Thus, without burning talismans or pacing the Dipper, a gust of wind swept by, and a deity descended, clad in golden helmet and armor, standing in the peach garden. “What task does the Dharma Master require of me?” he asked.

Upon seeing the Red Calamity Marshal descend, Ren Taohua swiftly closed her eyes and said, “Lord Zhou Qian, the fortune-teller, has recklessly revealed heavenly secrets. Though I have twice thwarted his schemes, he remains unrepentant, refusing to mend his ways and avert celestial wrath. Now, with malice in his heart, he has deceived me with false kinship, secretly dispatching the Black Calamity Marshal to lie in wait at the gate, intending to strike me down the moment I board the bridal palanquin! I have no choice but to enlist your divine power for protection. When the time comes, if the Black Calamity Deity raises his steel whip, I beg you to intercept it with your golden whip. Only after I have safely departed in the palanquin may you escort the Black Calamity Deity back to his post. Disobey, and you shall face the penalties decreed in the celestial tome!”

Peach Blossom Maiden cast her incantation, and the Red Calamity Deity vanished with the wind. Miss Ren slowly bound her raven tresses, then blew a breath of immortal qi upon the painted halberd—whereupon it once more became a slender peach sapling. Breaking three tender branches from the tree and one from the willow, she carried them back to her embroidered chamber. There, she fashioned a small bow and three arrows, setting them aside. Next, she took several strands of cotton thread, crossing them left and right in the pattern of a sieve, weaving warp and weft with meticulous care. Having consecrated them with a dharma seal, she gathered all the items together.

As the hour approached mid-morning, the sound of drums and music reached the gate, their resonant clamor filling the air. Suddenly, Elder Ren and his wife, both clad in auspicious robes, hurried in and called out, “Daughter! The Zhou family’s bridal palanquin has arrived—what will you do now?”

Peach Blossom Maiden, hearing this, could not help but shed tears. “Father, Mother! You have raised this daughter for sixteen years in vain. Today, when I go to the Zhou household, they will never accept me. A fierce battle awaits, and whether I live or die cannot be foretold. Yet there are a few words I must say—both of you must heed them well!”

Elder Ren and his wife had already begun weeping bitterly. “Do not fret so, my child,” they said. “Go forth with ease in your heart; surely Zhou Gong’s sorcery cannot overcome yours. Speak your mind plainly—what is it you wish to say? We, your parents, will grant whatever you ask.” Then the maiden began to recite:
