"Where neither yin nor yang reaches its end,
Do not say that doing good bears no fruit.
Though childless now, a son shall come in time—
When fate arrives, even daylight takes flight!
Riding twin clouds of wood to jade palaces,
The hour of *zi*, *wu*, *jia*, *wu* marks the appointed day.
Not a thread deviates from heaven and earth’s decree—
The Peach Garden has long awaited the lone parasol tree.
Thus is revealed the joy of doing good in the human realm!"

This foretells how Elder Ren and his wife shall one day ascend in broad daylight to become the celestial guardians of the Peach Garden. But this is the denouement’s tale, and no more shall be said of it.

When Peach Blossom Maiden finished speaking, she added, “The hour of *si* has arrived—this daughter must now prepare. Father, Mother, do not grieve!” Yet how could Elder Ren and his wife restrain themselves? The two elders stepped forward, clasping their daughter’s hands, and wept aloud.

At this moment of bitter parting, a maidservant announced, “Master Peng has come!” Hearing this, the couple stifled their sobs and looked up to see Peng Jian entering. He addressed them, saying, “Uncle, Aunt, kind cousin—cease your lamentations. I have something to report.”

Elder Ren, upon seeing him, flared with anger: “Peng Jian! Are you a man of honor? My daughter repeatedly charged you not to speak, yet you have let it slip, allowing Zhou Gong to record this grudge and forge this enmity. Now he uses this ruse of marriage to ensnare my daughter! He has no true son—he only waits for my child to depart before plotting against her. If my daughter returns unharmed, so be it; but if any mishap befalls her, I shall stake this old life of mine to settle accounts with you and Zhou Gong both. There can be no peace between us!”

Peng Jian, hearing this, flushed crimson with distress, stamping his feet as he protested, “I never spoke outright that day! Zhou Gong questioned me again and again, even striking me hundreds of times, yet I refused to reveal anything. Finally, in a rage, he drew his sword, threatening to kill me—I had no choice but to confess. He then punished me, forbidding me to leave, so I could not come to inform you. My offense is grave as the heavens, and now I see he has used this marriage ruse…”

Before Peng Jian could finish, Peach Blossom Maiden interjected, “Father, Mother, do not blame him wrongly.” Then, turning to Peng Jian, she said, “Brother, Zhou Gong sent you here—this is no time for idle talk. I have matters of great weight to entrust to you; you must follow my instructions to the letter.”

“I have some items to entrust to you.” With that, she quickly fetched a bow and arrows, handing them to Peng Jian and saying, “Take these and keep them on you. When my bridal sedan enters the gate, you must act thus and so.” Peng Jian nodded repeatedly. She then gave him a sieve made of thread, whispering further instructions. Peng Jian took it, slipped it out discreetly, and placed it inside the sedan chair. Peach Blossom Maiden, carrying the various items, wore a pearl crown adorned with eight treasures, a crimson python robe, and a pair of yellow satin Daoist shoes, refusing to let them touch the ground—she stood upon the kang, fastening her jade belt.

Just then, Matchmaker Jiang arrived and entered the main hall. She presented a three-foot length of red silk, a pair of treasure vases filled with the five grains. Peach Blossom Maiden instructed her to drape the red silk over her head and carry one vase in each hand. Silently, she mused, *“This woman’s heart is crooked—I shall use her in my stead this time.”* Then she called out, “Auntie Jiang, do not leave my side. Tomorrow, when you come to my home, I will reward you with twenty taels of silver.” Delighted, Matchmaker Jiang replied, “Miss, this old woman is here to assist you into your new home—how could I dare accept the master’s reward?” Master Ren said, “As long as you carefully support her, once my daughter has crossed over, I will give you twenty taels of silver—my word is true.” Then the young lady called for her father to lift her into the sedan chair.

The implements and objects Peach Blossom Maiden had used that day were originally meant to subdue and dispel malevolent spirits. Yet later generations, in nearly all wedding processions, followed this same form and practice, until it became an established custom and essential ritual.

In an instant, Master Ren carried Peach Blossom Maiden away, weeping loudly: “My child! Though your old father carries you out today, may you live as long as your parents, come of age in full health, enjoy a hundred years of marital harmony, see your descendants flourish, and know boundless fortune and longevity—nothing ill shall touch you.” Mistress Ren followed close behind, accompanying them for a stretch before breaking into loud sobs. Such was the sorrow of mother and daughter parting, a grief too deep to bear. Moreover, she had no sons, only this daughter, and now, with this farewell, she knew not whether fortune or misfortune awaited—her anguish was unbearable. Her wailing moved even Old Peng to shed a few tears.

Miss Peach Blossom was carried into the bridal sedan by Master Ren and had just taken her seat when suddenly a gust of eerie wind blew toward the palanquin. A steel whip lashed out—it was the Black Baleful Spirit, summoned by Master Zhou, striking the moment she boarded. But from the left, a golden whip flew forth, parrying the steel one, and the Red Baleful Spirit revealed his true form. Seeing his whip blocked, the Black Baleful Spirit cried, “I was sent by Magistrate Zhou under the authority of the Celestial Stem and Earthly Branch to strike down Ren’s Peach Blossom Maiden. Why does Your Excellency interfere with your golden whip and rescue this girl? Now I cannot fulfill my command—what am I to do?”

The Red Baleful Spirit replied with a conciliatory smile, “I, too, was summoned by Peach Blossom’s master, the Qi-True Man, under divine incantation to save her. The two of them are locked in a contest of yin and yang, of wit and strategy, yet ultimately, Peach Blossom acts in accord with the Dao. She was dispatched by the Jade Decree to descend to the mortal realm, provoking Master Zhou to contend with her so that both may return to their origins and avoid falling into the dust of the world. Their reunion is not far off—why should we two obey their private summons and risk discord?”

The Black Baleful Spirit, hearing this, said, “Your Excellency’s words align deeply with the profound and wondrous Dao.”

"Return each to your proper station." At once, the two spirits mounted the clouds and ascended to heaven. What transpired thereafter shall be revealed in the next chapter.

**Chapter Four, Episode Thirteen: The Wicked Contends with the Righteous—Divine Beings Act Without Partiality; True and False Yin-Yang Follow Their Course**

To continue: When Miss Ren Taohua’s bridal sedan arrived at Master Zhou’s gate, the Red and Black Baleful Spirits manifested their presence—one upholding Master Zhou’s celestial *Tian Gang* orthodox dharma to strike down Miss Taohua, the other obeying Miss Ren and the Qi-True Man’s divine incantation to shield and rescue her. The two divine beings having clarified their origins, they promptly mounted the clouds and returned each to their proper station.

Only Miss Taohua’s bridal sedan proceeded forth from the gate, drums and music resounding to the heavens, flutes and pipes filling the road. Countless servants cleared the way before and behind, their saddled steeds adorned with carved saddles. The townsfolk lining the streets, seeing that Master Zhou—a retired minister—was taking a bride, marveled at the sedan bedecked in silks and brocades, embroidered with the eighteen grotto-heavens’ immortals encircling it, its frame wrapped in red satin. Truly, it dazzled the eye, and all exclaimed, “The gentry and the common folk are worlds apart!” Some, knowing Master Zhou had no son, remarked, “A second wife, of course, must be grandly received!” Hearing this from within her sedan, Taohua seethed with resentment: “Were it not for my destined encounter with Zhou Qian, how could I avenge today’s humiliation?” Along the route, the eighteen grotto immortals’ effigies kept all malevolent spirits at bay, so Taohua remained unharmed.

When the sedan reached the Zhou residence, Ren household servants instructed the matchmaker Jiang: “Quickly, summon the Zhou family to perform the sedan incense ritual!” Jiang entered and relayed the message to Master Zhou. After the incense ritual, Zhou asked Jiang, “When you saw Ren Taohua board the sedan, did you hear any unusual sounds?” Jiang replied, “This humble woman stood nearby and saw her parents carry her into the sedan—there was no sound at all.” Hearing this, Zhou was astonished and said, “How strange! It seems this Taohua’s powers are no small matter.”

Even the Black Death Marshal could not touch her—what use were the lesser malevolent spirits outside the gate? Yet he had secretly summoned the Funeral Gate and Mourning Guest deities to flank her, to see what dark arts or powers this yin-born woman might wield to break his spells.

Turning to the matchmaker Jiang, he said, “Since she insists my servants perform the sedan incense ritual, why should I not do it myself? Attendants, quickly bring me the iron and heat it. Place cypress leaves and rue inside—let me purify the sedan so this yin-born woman may enter!”

His servants had already prepared the items; they handed them to Master Zhou, who seized them and rushed outside. Circling the bridal sedan three times, he remained unaware that cypress and rue were banes to evil spirits—within moments, the wailing specters and all manner of malevolent forces had fled, unable to stand their ground. Only Miss Taohua, hearing Zhou perform the ritual himself, could not help but smile in secret. “What a fool this Zhou Qian is!” she thought. “He does not even know that cypress and rue dispel all manner of evil spirits.”

This alone proved Zhou’s inferiority to Taohua: every item she employed was meant to counter his malevolent forces, yet Zhou understood none of it. He merely assumed Taohua possessed some power to subdue the spirits, unaware of the mutual generation and restraint among all things.

Once Zhou finished purifying the sedan, he strode back inside, tossed the iron and its contents aside, and ordered, “All bystanders, stand clear! Wait until the bride dismounts in the main hall before you—” His intent was clear: knowing he had set a vicious trap, he expected Taohua to reveal her own arts the moment she stepped into the hall. He wished to display his own prowess while settling the score for her repeated dismantling of his eight trigrams. Today, he fully expected Taohua to perish inside the sedan, and would later spread word that the master’s command had been to halt only at the main hall, where the sedan was to be carried.

However, Peng Jian had received Taohua’s transmitted arts and now oversaw the sedan-bearers. As they lifted the sedan, he strode ahead, positioning himself at the gate with his back to the outside and face toward the courtyard. Drawing a willow bow and a peachwood arrow, he nocked the arrow, raised the bow, and cried aloud:

*Willow bow, peachwood arrow,
Strike the left door, then the right,
Funeral Gate and Mourning Guest vanish without a trace,
All malevolent spirits flee from sight.*

As Peng Jian nocked the arrow and recited the incantation, he loosed it straight at the center of the gate. The Funeral Gate and Mourning Guest deities, most vulnerable to these implements, could not endure the twang of the bowstring—they instantly ascended on clouds, returning to their posts. This is why, in later ages, households would hang willow bows and peachwood arrows above their gates during inauspicious years.

At that moment, the Duke of Zhou believed that Peach Blossom Girl could never drive away the two malevolent deities, and that she was surely doomed. Thus, he secretly slipped out to observe from the side, even personally wielding an iron to circle her palanquin—though this was merely a pretext to step out. Little did he know he had already fallen into Peach Blossom Girl’s calculations!

Just as Peng Jian loosed his first arrow, delighted by its strike, he prepared to fire a second. Unexpectedly, the arrow flew straight toward the Duke of Zhou’s face. Quick-eyed, the Duke cried, *"Ill fortune!"* and dodged, barely avoiding it as it grazed past his ear. Enraged, he roared, *"Who dares act so recklessly, firing arrows here!"* Glancing up, he saw Peng Jian holding a small bow and shouted, *"How dare you, Peng Jian! To loose an arrow at me in secret!"*

Startled by the rebuke, Peng Jian hastily dropped the bow and replied, *"How could I be so bold? This was at Miss Ren’s command—she instructed me to shoot at the left and right gates, saying that Your Grace had summoned the two guests of Funeral Gate and Mourning Guest to lie in wait there, intending to harm her. She bade me fire these arrows to drive away the two baleful stars so she might alight from her palanquin and enter safely. I was but following orders; it has nothing to do with me!"*

Hearing this, the Duke of Zhou gasped, *"Alas!"* He swiftly calculated on his fingers, stamping his feet as he exclaimed, *"Disaster! All my painstaking efforts have been in vain—I have ruined my own scheme!"*

"Leave at once."

At this, the Duke of Zhou entered the inner hall and sat down, musing to himself: *"Though the baleful stars of Funeral Gate and Mourning Guest have been thwarted by this yin-born woman, many other malevolent spirits still gather here—what countermeasure will she employ now?"*

Meanwhile, Peach Blossom Maiden had alighted from her bridal palanquin. A matchmaker supported her as she stepped onto the red felt laid across the halls, inside and out. Clad in golden satin slippers that touched no earth, she walked slowly forward. Just as she neared the second gate, she saw Peng Jian retrieve a sieve woven of thread from the embroidered palanquin. Hurrying to her side, he tossed it high with both hands, lowering it to enshroud the beauty’s head as he recited the incantation:

*"Thread-woven sieve becomes the net of heaven,
Red felt binds the tripping rope tight.
The saddle bridles the star-and-sun steed,
Sheep flee at the sight of mortal grass—gone without trace!"*

As Peng Jian chanted the verse taught by Peach Blossom Maiden, he reached the second gate and scooped handfuls of straw from a square measure, scattering it in all directions. Seizing the moment, Peach Blossom Maiden swiftly stepped over the saddle, then drew a precious vase from her person. From it she poured five grains onto the ground.

Truly:
*To mortals, it seems but a trifling act,
Yet to immortals, its power is manifest.*

Thus Peach Blossom Maiden proceeded to the great inner hall. By now, all the maidservants and matrons of the Zhou household knew that the Duke had sought to slay Miss Ren with sorcery the moment she stepped from her palanquin. Seeing her unharmed, they realized her magic was the greater, and the Duke’s schemes had been undone. Hearing further from Lady Jiang of her beauty—so fair it could sink fish and shame geese, a visage of celestial grace—who would not crowd close to glimpse her? The great inner hall was soon packed so densely that the yin qi grew overwhelming.

The malevolent spirits, restrained all along by Peach Blossom Maiden’s arts, dared not approach. Seeing her pass the critical position and the yin qi swell further—many women present being impure—the spirits feared contamination by defilement, lest they be barred from returning to their posts. Thus they mounted the clouds and departed, each to their proper place.

When the Duke of Zhou saw Peach Blossom Maiden enter unscathed, passing through three gates to reach the inner hall in perfect safety, his Three Corpses seethed with fury, smoke rising from his seven orifices. He cursed aloud: *"What formidable skill this yin-born woman possesses! She has undone my sorcery at every turn. Our enmity runs deep—I swear I shall never coexist with such a one!"*

Hearing Matchmaker Jiang call out, *"The Ren family’s people insist on summoning the groom to perform the bows—what is to be done?"* the Duke of Zhou grew frantic, wringing his hands in helplessness. *"What plan can I devise now?"* he muttered to himself. After a moment’s thought, finding no recourse, he reluctantly ordered his beloved daughter, Miss Tianxiang, to stand in as the groom. *"Quickly, send the maids to fetch my daughter!"* Then he summoned the housekeeper and instructed her thus and so.

The housekeeper approached Peach Blossom Maiden and said, *"His Lordship says today is an inauspicious day, and the groom must not meet the bride. He has sent my young lady to perform the bows in his stead, temporarily taking the groom’s place to enter the bridal chamber."*

Peach Blossom Maiden listened, inwardly delighted: *"Now I have a substitute—I need not expend further effort!"* She stood still, handing the precious vase to Matchmaker Jiang. Secretly, she drew a bronze mirror from the brocade pouch at her breast and tucked it into her sleeve, raising both hands in a dignified bow, her plan already set.

Presently, Miss Tianxiang entered, the air filled with the resounding clamor of drums and music. The two beauties exchanged bows and courtesies before performing the wedding rites. A retinue of maids followed them into the bridal chamber.

Once inside, Miss Tianxiang lifted the red silk veil from Peach Blossom Maiden’s face. Gazing upon her, she saw a vision no less radiant than a celestial maiden of the Jade Palace or the Moon Goddess Chang’e, and her heart swelled with admiration. *"Alas!"* she sighed inwardly, *"what a pity—such a thousandfold beauty, doomed to die by my father’s schemes. How pitiful!"*

Peach Blossom Maiden, in turn, regarded Miss Tianxiang and thought:
*Her brows curve like crescent moons, her eyes shine bright as autumn stars,
Adorned with jeweled hairpins, her grace outshines all others—
A single glance reveals her tender charm.*

*"What a rare beauty!"* Peach Blossom Maiden mused. *"A face seldom seen among mortals. Yet how tragic—tonight she will die in my place!"* Both maidens shared a silent sorrow, their hearts aligned, though neither would perish—of this, more later.

Miss Tianxiang spoke first: *"Sister Ren, please come and sit upon the bridal bed."*

How would Peach Blossom Maiden respond? Could she evade the White Tiger Star lurking there? For that, await the next chapter.

**Chapter Fourteen: Peach Blossom Maiden Uses the Dao to Break the Dao—The Duke of Zhou Plots Harm but Meets His Own Demise**

Peach Blossom Maiden and Miss Tianxiang, having met, each felt a tender pity and affection for the other. Yet Peach Blossom, being a celestial maiden born of the Daoist arts, understood all that had passed and all that was to come. Tonight, though compelled by circumstance, she would let Miss Tianxiang take her place.

Thus, she gave a cold laugh and said to the young lady: *"You are the honored guest—pray, take the seat of honor."*

Miss Tianxiang replied, *"Then I shall keep you company."*

Miss Tianxiang said, *"Sister, you are my elder—tonight I merely stand in for my brother. How could I presume to take the seat of honor?"*

Peach Blossom Maiden said, *"Since you presume to take your brother’s place, you are the bridegroom in his stead and should sit first."*

Miss Tianxiang, knowing her father intended hidden harm against her yet lacking any means of escape, was compelled by necessity. Eager to see the matter done so she might return to her chambers, she remained unaware of the peril in the seating’s orientation. Seeing the logic in Peach Blossom’s words, she said, *"In that case, I shall defer to you, Sister—pray forgive my presumption in sitting first."* She then moved to take the upper seat upon the bed.

Peach Blossom Maiden swiftly drew the embroidered curtain to shield herself, while silently reciting the incantation to summon the spirits. The White Tiger Marshal was roused, and with a gust of raging wind, revealed his true form. That fierce and malevolent star was truly formidable! Seeing a yin-person seated upon the bed, he let out a roar and lunged—biting deep into Miss Tianxiang’s shoulder.

Alas!

In an instant, the tender blossom met with a sudden storm—who could have foreseen the fragile bud would encounter such a violent gale! At that moment, Miss Tianxiang cried out *"Ai-yo!"* and tumbled from the bed, blood streaming from her mouth. The women below witnessed this and were struck with terror! They rushed forward to lift her, only to find her face ashen as gold paper, fresh blood flowing from her lips—already stiff and lifeless. The women called to her in vain, their wails growing louder and louder. Someone hurried to report to Lord Zhou.

Lord Zhou, hearing the sudden lamentations from the chamber, assumed Peach Blossom had fallen to his scheme, and that the Jia household was now in mourning—his heart swelled with joy. But then came the messenger’s report: *"The young lady has collapsed and died for no reason in the bridal chamber!"* At first, Lord Zhou refused to believe it, but upon hearing these words, he felt as though he had lost his footing on a high ridge or capsized in the Yangzi—he dashed to the bridal chamber, cradled his daughter in his arms, and wailed, *"Why has she died here today, so suddenly and without cause?"*

Peach Blossom, upon hearing this, let out a faint, cold laugh. *"Lord Zhou! Who do you think you’re trying to frighten with your daughter? Such words may deceive the foolish, but how could they ever fool me?"*

"Last night, you summoned the White Tiger inauspicious star to bite her to death—that’s why she bled just now. A fine young lady, ruined by your own sorcery, and now you weep?" Upon hearing this, Lord Zhou flushed with shame and fury, his lamentations stilled.

He raised his gaze to regard Peach Blossom, seeing her:
Clad in crimson from head to toe,
Her celestial charm rivaled the immortals’ grace.
At first glance, Lord Zhou mistook her for some ancient scholar’s refined beauty—
But now, beholding her eyes like autumn waters and her bones of jade, he could not help but falter: *"No wonder this yin-born wretch is so formidable—her very appearance sets her apart!"*

Swallowing his pride, he forced a smile and addressed her: *"Miss Ren, you understand this matter, while I remain in the dark. Might there be some divine method to revive my daughter?"*

Peach Blossom laughed. *"Lord Zhou, your study of the *Tian Gang* formulas was not in vain—yet how is it you know only how to cast spells, not how to break them? Instead of blaming others for disrupting your *Tian Gang* Eight Trigrams, should you not fault your own lack of skill and imprecise Daoist arts? Since you now seek my aid, reviving your daughter is no difficulty. Fetch me counterflow water from the river and willow branches, and I shall perform a minor technique before your eyes—she will revive at once, leaving you utterly convinced!"*

What is counterflow water? When the great sea rises in tide, the small river ebbs; when the small river rises, the great sea ebbs. Taking the small river’s rising tide—with the great sea as reference—this is counterflow water.

Lord Zhou found Peach Blossom’s words grating, but with his daughter’s life at stake, he dared not argue. He immediately ordered his servants: *"Quickly, fetch counterflow water and willow branches!"* In the time it took to exhale, both were brought before him.

Peach Blossom had a cool bamboo mat laid upon the ground. They lifted Lady Tianxiang onto it, positioning her supine, and barred all idle chatter. Unhurried, she took several willow twigs, dipped them in the counterflow water, swirling them thrice to the left and thrice to the right. Then, with mudras and incantations, she flicked the water from the willow onto Tianxiang’s face. Truly, the wonders of an immortal’s craft: after three recitations and three sprinkles, Tianxiang’s three *hun* and seven *po* returned to her body, her *qi* reversed its course, and she returned to the living. *"Ah!"* she gasped, *"How terrifying!"* Her apricot eyes flew open, and with a roll, she slowly sat up on the mat, dazed.

Every servant and maid rejoiced, marveling: *"Miss Ren’s arts reach the divine—she truly possesses the power to raise the dead!"* Lord Zhou, his face burning with humiliation, had no choice but to step forward and bow in gratitude to Peach Blossom.

When Tianxiang revived and saw that it was Peach Blossom who had saved her, her heart brimmed with endless gratitude. She knelt to thank her for the gift of life, then, without returning to her own chambers, remained by Peach Blossom’s side in the bridal room. The two, kindred spirits drawn to one another, admired each other deeply—both of the same age, their bond was one of perfect harmony. But of this, no more shall be said.

Lord Zhou, overwhelmed with shame that day, sat alone in his study, brooding in silence: *"Today, all those malevolent spirits and fierce deities were thwarted by that yin-born woman—only to have the White Tiger Star’s general bite my daughter to death. Though she was revived by Peach Blossom’s hand, I despise how she flaunted her abilities, humiliating me before all those women! My original plan to deceive her into marriage failed to kill her, and now she sits safely in my estate. Moreover, in three days’ time, she will meet the groom—what can I possibly offer her? I must devise a fatal scheme to eliminate this yin-born woman. First, to rid myself of this worry; second, to vent the hatred in my heart!"*

He hastily retrieved *The Divine Book of Heavenly Stems* and, after obtaining Peach Blossom’s birth date and hour, meticulously calculated her life’s fate. Upon careful divination, he discovered the method of *"Black Hound Suppression"*—a technique with no possible countermeasure. Lifting his head, he chuckled, *"Had I known this was the fire, the rice would have cooked long ago! If I had used this method earlier, I would have spared myself so much frustration!"*

With that, he put away *The Divine Book of Heavenly Stems* and stepped into the outer hall, summoning a servant: *"Take a string of copper coins and immediately purchase a black female hound from the due south. Bring it to the rear garden for use—do not delay."* The servant received his orders and departed. Before long, the black hound was bought and delivered to the garden’s keepers.

The night passed without incident. The next day, Lord Zhou summoned Peng Jian and instructed him: *"Go to Squire Ren’s rear garden, where there is a worm-eaten peach tree. Select a branch from the due south side, chop off a large one, and bring it to me—I have use for it. Carry it straight here without turning your head to look back! If you dare glance back, your eyes will be blinded. Do not say I did not warn you."* Peng Jian received his orders, hurried to Squire Ren’s estate, and informed the squire. In the rear garden, he chose a towering peach tree and hacked off a branch from the southern side, then rushed back to the manor.

Lord Zhou was overjoyed. *"Is this the southern branch?"* he asked. *"Good. Take it to the rear garden."* Peng Jian carried the peach branch and followed Lord Zhou to the garden, where the black hound was led out. Lord Zhou ordered a ritual table set with offerings of flowers, fruit, incense, and candles. He snapped the peach branch in two, dipped it in cinnabar, and inscribed Peach Blossom’s birth date and hour upon it. Wrapping it in yellow paper, he had it tied to the black hound’s body, then bent the branch into a loop and fastened it around the hound’s neck. With the peach branch, he drew seven talismanic seals, personally hanging them on the loop before his hands traced mudras and his lips murmured incantations—seven times over. He then peeled off the talismans, burned them with fire, and removed the inscribed branch and loop, reducing all to ashes. At once, he had the black hound struck dead. The servants were ordered to bury it in the due south of the rear garden, and the offerings were cleared away. Lord Zhou burst into laughter: *"Wretched woman! Now let’s see how you escape me!"*

It so happened that the peach branch was Peach Blossom’s life-root; by cutting it first, Lord Zhou had already subdued her vital mechanism. Peng Jian, standing outside, had secretly watched the proceedings. Seeing Lord Zhou’s elaborate ritual, he grew suspicious; when he heard the lord’s cold, triumphant words, his heart sank. *"This is bad!"* he thought. *"He truly means to harm Miss Ren! I must hurry and warn her so she can prepare!"* As an old minister long in Lord Zhou’s service, Peng Jian moved freely through the manor, unchallenged. He rushed straight to Peach Blossom’s bridal chamber.

Meanwhile, ever since Peach Blossom had revived Miss Tianxiang, the latter, deeply grateful and perfectly matched in temperament, had scarcely left her side. The two chatted and laughed together until the third watch before retiring to their rooms. That day, as Peach Blossom was dressing early in the rear pavilion, Miss Ren sat alone in her chamber, pondering how to return home. Suddenly, she was seized by a fit of dread, her flesh crawling. Hastily, she calculated with her fingers and understood at once. *"Lord Zhou has cut my life-root!"* she cried in alarm. *"He’s using the Black Hound Suppression method against me, and he has my birth date and hour. Even if I had the powers of an immortal, I could not escape this calamity. What am I to do?"* She was lost in distress when suddenly Peng Jian rushed in.

Before his feet had even steadied, he gasped for breath and cried, "Dear sister and benefactor, today is ill-fated—great disaster has come!" He then recounted in full detail how Lord Zhou had once more performed his arts in the rear garden, preparing to subdue her, and how he had ordered him to cut peach branches for the purpose.

Peach Blossom replied calmly, "Brother, do not fret. I already knew of this. This is called the Black Hound Suppression, a venomous scheme of demonic arts. Yet this time, I fear I cannot escape this calamity—my life is surely forfeit! But recall how I saved you before; now, I ask that you save me in return!"

Upon hearing this, Peng Jian hastily replied, "If there is any way I, Peng Jian, can serve you, sister, I would plunge into boiling water or tread upon fire, and ten thousand deaths would not deter me!"

Peach Blossom, hearing his words, rejoiced greatly. "Good," she said, "then my younger sister is out of danger." How she would break the spell, however, remains to be seen in the next chapter.

**Chapter Fifteen: Peach Blossom Thrice Unravels the Celestial Stem Method; Zhou Qian Again Deploys a Demon-Suppressing Scheme**

*Poem:*
Yin and yang reverse in ceaseless flux,
Their clash dims the sun and moon’s bright luster.
The common folk gaze upward, lost in dread,
While mighty Heaven departs its clouded realm.
Hand in hand with sun and moon, one ascends to paradise,
Standing serene beside the Emperor’s throne.
How resplendent, how pure—beyond earthly garb,
All things rejoice in harmony, raising cups of rhinoceros horn.

Now, Zhou Gong had employed the Black Hound Suppression to bring about Peach Blossom’s death. Peng Jian, desperate, asked how she might be saved. Peach Blossom replied, “This is a demonic art—even the highest immortals of the Great Luo Heaven would struggle to escape its bonds. It severs the three hun-souls from the body and scatters the seven po-souls to the void. There is no doubt: this is a death from which there is no return.

But, dear brother Peng, recall how I saved you yesterday. Today, I ask that you repay that kindness and rescue me.”

Peng Jian, frantic, stamped his foot and cried, “If I had the power to save you, I would not need to tell you—I would have already broken his spell and rescued you!”

Peach Blossom said, “I do not ask you to break his spell. Only follow my words, and I will be saved.”

Hearing this, Peng Jian rejoiced. “Whatever you command, how could I dare ignore it? See how I did not fail in a single task you entrusted to me yesterday. Speak quickly, so I may go and fetch—”

Peach Blossom continued, “You heard Zhou Gong’s order to cut down the peach tree at my home. That tree is my life-root; if you sever it, it will be as if you’ve dammed the source of a river. Even if I could transform or take flight, it would be of no use. Tomorrow at the *wei* hour, my death will come.”

Peng Jian sighed. “How can this be? I am but a fool, untrained in the arcane arts. Otherwise, even if he commanded me to die, I would not go!”

Peach Blossom said, “There is no use in regret now. Tomorrow at the *wei* hour, my death is certain. But I have devised a way to escape it: after I die, Zhou Gong will surely have me encoffined at once. When they lift my body to place me in the coffin, do not wait until I am inside before acting. The moment they begin to raise me, take three wooden staves and bar the door. Strike the bolt three times, then cry out loudly, ‘Peach Blossom!’ Kick the door open with your right foot, and I will revive by my own wondrous means. Do not fail in this!”

Peng Jian replied, “The timing must be exact—neither too early nor too late. You must watch closely and act the moment they lift me.”

“Just think—how far is it from here to the main gate? By the time I run there, you may already have been encoffined for some time. How can that work?”

Peach Blossom replied, “Brother, you are right. In my haste, I did not explain clearly. When the hour of *shen* arrives, you may go ahead and wait outside the main gate. When you hear a gust of fragrant wind pass by, that will be the moment they lift me. Then you must act swiftly, just as I instructed!”

Peng Jian nodded and said, “If the timing is precise, what difficulty could there be? But if there is no fragrant wind, do not blame me!”

Peach Blossom assured him, “It will certainly come.”

Peng Jian, still half-doubting, replied, “If the fragrant wind truly serves as the sign, then you may rest easy—I will take full responsibility!” With that, he hurriedly took his leave and departed.

Peach Blossom, alone in her chamber, prepared the magical talismans she would need to protect herself after death. She placed each one into a brocade pouch and fastened them to her innermost garments. Just as she finished, Miss Tianxiang, having completed her morning toilette, entered the room. The two exchanged courtesies and sat down to converse. Peach Blossom did not breathe a word of her father’s dark schemes, instead laughing and chatting as if nothing were amiss, until evening fell.

Miss Tianxiang dined with Peach Blossom before taking her leave to retire to her own chamber. As for Peach Blossom, she did not close her eyes all night, sitting on her bed with her eyes shut to rest her spirit. When dawn came, she rose, washed, and dressed, forgoing her usual hairpins and jewels. Instead, she coiled her hair in a Daoist style and donned a pale green Daoist robe, her demeanor cheerful and unburdened, revealing nothing.

That day, Zhou Gong remained uneasy. He secretly sent someone to observe her, and the messenger returned to report that her countenance showed no sign of distress, nor had she made any unusual movements. Upon hearing this, Zhou Gong rejoiced, saying, “This time, I have suppressed her life-star—she is surely dazed and powerless!”

When noon arrived, he hurried to the rear garden, inscribed a hastening-death talisman, and began pacing the Dipper steps as he intoned the incantation. Just as he finished burning the talisman, Peach Blossom and Miss Tianxiang were in the boudoir, deep in conversation, when suddenly Peach Blossom cried out and collapsed to the floor. Miss Tianxiang and the maidservants, unaware of the cause, were startled and rushed forward to help her up.

Seeing her breath entirely stilled and her body limp as silk, she appeared beyond all hope of life. Truly:

While three inches of qi serve a thousand uses,
Once the last breath departs, all affairs cease.

At the sight, Miss Tianxiang was so stricken that her limbs failed her. She burst into loud sobs, crying, “Sister! How could you, so sound and well, suddenly perish without cause? Alas, your youth, your moon-bright face and flower-like beauty—now you are gone forever. How can this not rend the heart?” She stroked the lifeless form, her grief sharp and piercing. The maidservants all began to weep, their wails rising like the heavens splitting and the earth cracking.

Peng Jian hurried into the room, equally stunned. “Truly, what fearsome sorcery! The exact hour of *wei*—not a moment’s deviation!” In his haste, he glanced over and saw Peach Blossom lying on the ground, her complexion still as in life, only her lips tightly clenched. Overcome, he too began to wail. Then, suddenly recollecting himself, he muttered, “Why am I weeping here? I must hurry to the main gate and wait—saving her life is the only matter of consequence!”

Rubbing away the tears from her eyes, she rushed out the main gate to wait. Word soon reached Duke Zhou. Overjoyed at the news, he personally strode into the chamber. Seeing Peach Blossom indeed lifeless, he sneered, “Wretch! Can you still escape my grasp now?”

Lady Tianxiang, her eyes brimming with tears, pleaded, “Father, though Ren Taohua has offended you and deserves death, remember how he saved your daughter’s life. Show him mercy—spare him a little, and revive him if you can!”

Duke Zhou laughed. “What do you, a child, know of such things? This is fate already sealed—who could bring him back?” He then ordered his servants, “Ren Taohua died at the third quarter of the *wei* hour, his baleful influence too heavy to linger. Waste no time—prepare his funeral at once. Seal the coffin swiftly! Afterward, send word to the Ren household and choose a day for the burial. Place him in the small room to the right of the main hall. No wailing from the women!” He further commanded the gatekeepers to bolt the doors, lest any of the Ren household’s maidservants slip away to deliver the news.

Little did he know that the gates had already been shut—too late to stop Peng Jian’s desperate efforts. Soon, all the funeral preparations were made, the necessary items laid out in the outer hall. Duke Zhou forbade anyone from changing Peach Blossom’s clothes and instead dispatched four maidservants to carry her body for the encoffining. The four maids, following orders, attempted to lift the corpse—yet no matter how they strained, it was as if dragonflies sought to shake a stone pillar. Not an inch could they budge it.

The onlookers gasped in astonishment: “How can such a slight frame be so impossibly heavy?” Seeing this, Duke Zhou added four more maids to the effort—yet still they could not lift her. Enraged, he bellowed, “This wretch played tricks in life, and even in death she dares defy me? All of you—help me lift her!” But no matter how many joined, it was futile. The maids strained until their breath came in ragged gasps, their bodies drenched in sweat, yet all cried, “We cannot move her!” Duke Zhou roared at them to stand aside and summoned forty of his strongest retainers.

The men strode forward, some gripping her head from either side, others seizing her feet, still more bracing her midsection—hands tangled in a frantic scramble, their shouts rising in confusion. “How bizarre! It’s as if she’s rooted to the earth—we cannot even sway her!” Duke Zhou’s fury erupted like thunder. Snatching his Heavenly Dipper sword, he swung it down upon Peach Blossom’s shoulder with a resounding *clang*—sparks flew, the hilt numbed his tiger’s mouth, and his hands stung with pain. “What an indestructible corpse!” he snarled. He hacked at her head and face again and again, yet not even her garments bore a single tear.

The retainers and maidservants exchanged stunned whispers: “This woman must have been a cultivator of the Dao—her body is incorruptible!” Hearing their awe only stoked Duke Zhou’s rage further. With a furious shout, he demanded, “Bring me dry kindling—now!” His attendants dared not delay, rushing to gather armfuls of wood. Duke Zhou ordered it piled upon Peach Blossom’s body, intending to burn her remains to ash.

One retainer knelt and ventured, “If we set fire, won’t it—”
Duke Zhou cut him off with a roar: “Fetch it at once! I have my methods—do you think I’d let the hall burn? Light the fire—now!”

The retainers swiftly fetched the kindling and ignited it beneath and around the corpse. Yet something uncanny occurred: though they lit it for some time, the flames would not catch, and if one side flickered to life, the other would immediately die out. Duke Zhou bellowed at his servants to add oil, drenching the wood, but the oil seemed only to smother the fire like water, extinguishing what little flame remained. Thick smoke billowed forth, choking Duke Zhou and his household until tears and mucus streamed down their faces, sending them scrambling into the courtyard to catch their breath.

Duke Zhou mused, “Carry the wood out first—we’ll burn her slowly. There must be some reason for this. Let me calculate and see what sorcery this yin-being has wrought to interfere.” He hastily began his divination, then sighed, “I was careless! She used the *Double-Body Technique* to protect her remains, fearing harm after death. Now, I shall summon the Six Ding spirits and invoke the gods—let’s see how this yin-being escapes *that*!”

With that, he unsheathed his *Celestial Stem Sword*, removed his golden crown, and let his hair fall loose. As he chanted incantations under his breath, the myriad deities were already alerted, descending upon Duke Zhou’s estate—though their golden forms remained invisible in daylight. Suddenly, a fragrant breeze swept through the hall, and Duke Zhou knew the gods had arrived. He ordered all but four of his attendants and maidservants to withdraw, declaring, “This time, just four men will be enough to lift her!”

Time seemed to stretch, but in an instant, Peng Jian, who had been waiting impatiently at the gate, grew anxious with doubt. Then, a sudden gust of fragrant wind assailed his senses, and he rejoiced, “The moment is here!” Swiftly, he struck the gate three times with his wooden staff and cried aloud, “Peach Blossom!”

Whether her power could truly break Duke Zhou’s spell remains to be seen in the next chapter.

**Chapter Sixteen: A Battle of Wits in the Realm of Yin and Yang—The Two Sages Return to Their True Forms**

At the first whiff of the fragrant breeze, Peng Jian followed Peach Blossom’s instructions precisely: he struck the gate thrice with his wooden staff and cried aloud, *“Peach Blossom!”* Then, lifting his right foot, he kicked once—*crack!*—and the gate swung open. Inside, Peach Blossom’s corpse had just been hoisted up and carried out of the chamber. Duke Zhou, overjoyed, hurried after them, urging, “Quickly now, take her to be encoffined!”

But Peach Blossom’s soul, held captive by the malevolent *sha*, could not reenter her body. The moment Peng Jian struck the gate, the *sha* was startled into retreat, and her spirit rushed back into her flesh, her essence restored to its rightful place. With a sudden twist, she rose to her feet.

The Six Ding and Six Jia deities, seeing the immortal maiden return to the yang realm, vanished in a flash of light, ascending back to heaven. The servants and maidservants, witnessing Miss Peach Blossom rise so abruptly, shrieked in terror, scattering in all directions: *“Disaster! Disaster!”* Chaos erupted.

Peach Blossom’s almond eyes flew open. Spotting Duke Zhou nearby, her fury flared. *“Zhou Qian! I share no blood feud with you—why must you resort to such cruelty, bent on killing me? What now can you do to me?”*

Duke Zhou, stung by shame and rage, brandished his Heavenly Stem Sword and lunged at her. But Peach Blossom swiftly recited the counter-spell of the *gou-sha*, stepping back as she flung her sleeves toward him. With a peal of laughter, the *sha* reversed its course, striking Duke Zhou unawares. Though he wielded great power, he had no time to react—*“Ah!”*—his sword clattered to the ground, and he collapsed in a heap, his own *fa-ming* turned against him by the backlash of *sha*. Unaware of the transformation in her sleeves, the recoil of the *sha* struck him down, claiming his life instead.

Truly:

The flames one kindles burn oneself first;
He who harms others harms himself before.
Alas, how few in this world grasp this truth!

In an instant, Duke Zhou crumpled to the ground, his face purple, his lips cyan, his breath stilled. The entire household erupted in panic—men and women alike wailed in grief, crying, *"The lord must have been struck down by Ren Taohua’s sorcery! Do not let her escape! Seize her and take her to Marshal Wen’s estate!"*

Meanwhile, Tianxiang, seeing her father refuse her pleas, wept bitterly as she withdrew to her chambers. Taohua, hearing the clamor, let out a cold laugh. *"Zhou Qian sought to kill others, yet perished by his own hand—this is his just retribution! I stand here now. Let them try to take me."*

Just then, Peng Jian, having finished his tasks, rushed inside. Hearing the wailing, he was alarmed. In a few strides, he reached the hall, only to find the household in uproar. There stood Taohua, smiling faintly. He hurried forward, calling, *"Dear sister, everyone rejoices that you live—"* Before he could finish, the crowd swarmed around him, shouting, *"The lord has been slain by Taohua! Why waste words with her?"*

Peng Jian froze in shock. *"Is this true?"* The crowd pointed to the body. He looked up—Duke Zhou lay motionless. He pressed a hand to his mouth: no breath remained. With a cry, he broke into sobs. The others consoled him, *"He is gone. Weeping will not help—we must act!"*

Peng Jian stifled his tears. *"What can we do? He sought to harm others, then turned on his own daughter, only to be saved by the very one he wronged. Even then, he did not repent. Now fate has claimed him—who can he beg for mercy?"* Turning to Taohua, he knelt before her. *"Dear sister, show compassion once more! We will be forever in your debt!"*

Taohua helped him rise. *"Brother, do not humble yourself. They mean to take me to Marshal Wen. Let them summon him—I fear him not!"*

Peng Jian pleaded, *"They are fools. Sister, for my sake, spare him."* With that, he knelt again. The crowd followed, prostrating themselves, wailing, *"Lady Ren, if you revive the lord, we will be grateful for generations!"*

Taohua, moved by their pleas and eager to display her skill, smiled faintly. *"You no longer wish to seize me? Very well—for Brother Peng’s sake, I shall try."* The crowd kowtowed, begging, *"How may we save him?"*

Taohua’s smile turned cold. *"Do as before. Simply call out, ‘*Jiedao*!’—and he will revive."*

Peng Jian frowned. *"Why not call his name? Why ‘*Jiedao*’?"*

*"That is a celestial secret—how could you understand?"* Taohua replied. *"Go now!"*

"Once your master revives, you shall see my skill." Hearing this, Peng Jian asked no further. He shut the great doors as instructed and performed the ritual as before, crying out, "*Jiedao!*" At once, Lord Zhou’s wandering soul awakened and returned to his body. With a roll, he sat up upon the ground. Seeing Taohua, his eyes burned with hatred toward his foe. He leapt to his feet, seized the Heavenly Stem Sword, and roared, "Wretched fiend, stay your steps! How dare you harm me with the *huisha* technique? If I do not slay you today, I am no man!" He lunged forward, sword in hand.

Taohua swiftly drew a peach branch of boundless efficacy from her brocade pouch. With jadelike hands, she parried his blade and shouted, "Zhou Qian, ungrateful wretch! Do you forget the debt of your revived life? How dare you turn your strength against me?" Lord Zhou struck again. Taohua dodged and countered with her peach branch, one yin, one yang, locked in combat across the great hall.

Peng Jian cried out in alarm, "This is ill!" Unarmed, how could he intervene? He rushed to inform Miss Tianxiang, who fainted in terror upon hearing the news. She then hurried to the Ren household to deliver the report.

Meanwhile, Lord Zhou and Taohua fought from the great doors to the courtyard. Finding the space too cramped to unleash their powers, they both rose upon clouds into the midair, clashing fiercely in a dance of attack and retreat.

By then, Old Master Ren had arrived at the Zhou residence. Miss Tianxiang emerged to meet him and recounted the events, dissolving into sobs. Together, they raised their eyes to the heavens and watched.

They watched as the two, enveloped in radiant clouds, waged a bitter and fierce battle in midair, fighting ever farther away until they gradually vanished from sight. The cries of a child calling for their father rang in their ears, yet neither paid the slightest heed.

Later, when Old Master Ren and his wife saw their daughter restored to her divine seat, and beheld Tianxiang—whose appearance was identical to their own child—learning from Peng Jian how well they had gotten along, the elderly couple felt a surge of compassion. They instructed Peng Jian to propose that Tianxiang be recognized as their daughter. Upon hearing that her father had ascended to godhood, and recalling her early loss of her mother with no one to rely upon, Tianxiang was moved by the Rens’ kind offer. Remembering, too, her bond with Taohua, she promptly visited the Ren household to pay her respects to the elderly couple. They then welcomed her to stay as a companion.

As for Lord Zhou’s household affairs, they were entrusted to Peng Jian for management. But these are matters for later.

Meanwhile, Lord Zhou and Taohua fought with ever greater vigor, each unleashing their full powers, stirring winds to howl and thunder to roar. Their battle soon alarmed the Celestial Censor on patrol, who saw how fiercely they clashed, nearly reaching the Northern Gate of Heaven. He hastened to report to the True Martial Emperor of the Northern Heavens, the Dark Warrior of the North. The Emperor surveyed them with his wisdom-eye and already knew their origins. He dispatched his generals, the Tortoise and the Serpent, to bring the two before the divine throne.

The Tortoise and Serpent Generals received the divine decree. Each intercepted the two combatants amid the clouds, shouting loudly: "Cease your struggle! We bear the Celestial Emperor’s command—you are summoned to the Golden Palace! Disobey, and our might shall cast you from the heavens!" Hearing the summons of the Emperor, the pair had no choice but to sheathe their weapons. Together with the Tortoise and Serpent Generals, they approached the august presence and prostrated themselves, kneeling in reverence. After kowtowing, the Emperor issued his jade decree:

"You both possess foundational Dao cultivation—why do you harm one another? Zhou Qian, you are the transformed essence of the Ruyi Precept Blade, once the divination page in the Tushita Palace. Yet you failed to uphold purity, descending to the mortal realm in secret to reveal celestial secrets, thereby dragging Peach Blossom Girl into the world below. Ren Taohua is none other than the Ruyi Blade’s scabbard. Your natures are one—do not entertain other intentions! Today marks the time for your physical forms to ascend. Each of you shall be granted a golden elixir."

"Command them to swallow the elixirs," the Emperor continued. "Should either of you now harbor deviant intentions, this pill within your belly shall not dissolve within three quarters of an hour—even a body as indestructible as vajra will melt into pus and blood!"

With these words, he unfurled his Seven-Star Banner, wrapping the two within its folds and bearing them to the Wudang Mountains, where they were appointed as generals—Marshals Zhou and Peach. With a surge of divine radiance, the two marshals took their places on either side, standing to left and right. The Emperor then waved his Seven-Star Precious Banner seven times and exhaled a breath of primordial true qi toward the two marshals. At once, they withdrew their divine radiance, and their physical forms returned to their proper state.

That night, the Daoist master Ye of Wudang Mountain dreamed that the two marshals had entrusted him with letters for their families. Upon waking and ascending to the main hall, he saw that among the celestial generals now stood two divine marshals, their awe-inspiring radiance dazzling, their golden light resplendent. Startled, he noticed that beneath each of their feet lay a book, every detail clearly inscribed. He retrieved them but dared not open them. Immediately, he paid homage to the Emperor and the golden forms of the two marshals before hastening down the mountain under the cover of night, making his way to Chaoge City.

Upon locating the Zhou residence, he handed the letters to the gatekeeper and recounted the dream in which the two marshals had appeared. The gatekeeper hurried inside to inform Peng Jian. Peng Jian received the letters and, as courtesy demanded, provided the Daoist with a meal. He then accompanied the master to personally inform Elder Ren and his wife, as well as Miss Tianxiang. Each opened their letters to read the contents, which spoke only of the need for harmony between the two families and words of comfort. All were overjoyed, remarking that though the two had become gods, their spiritual efficacy remained undiminished.

Thereupon, they traveled together with Daoist Ye to Wudang Mountain to offer incense. First, they paid homage to the Emperor, then bowed before the two marshals. Upon closer inspection, the golden visages of the two marshals appeared no different from their living countenances. After the group had paid their respects, they presented Daoist Ye with a hundred taels of gold to cover the costs of incense and lamp oil for the two marshals’ worship. They then returned home, and the tale spread far and wide, astonishing all who heard it.

Before long, word reached the imperial court, and not a single civil or military official failed to come and pay their respects. Their devotion in worship was met with swift and resonant responses. Later generations, reflecting on this passage, composed a poem in testimony. The poem reads:

**First Poem:**
To act with heaven as witness in all affairs,
Never presume past causes can deceive.
Good and evil meet their just reward—
Three feet above, the gods watch all we leave.

**Second Poem:**
All things are ordained by heaven’s decree,
Schemes unravel when their time is done.
A heart insatiable as serpents swallowing elephants—
Cultivate intent like sages, wise and true.
No remedy exists for vain desire,
No wealth can purchase immortality.
The world’s harsh ways evoke both ancient and modern sighs—
Let others do their worst; my heart stands firm.
